<a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_United_States.svg" class="image"><img alt="Flag of the United States.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/16px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="8" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/24px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/32px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1235" data-file-height="650" /></a> <a href="/wiki/Portal:United_States" title="Portal:United States">United States&#32;portal</a></td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:History_of_the_United_States" title="Template:History of the United States"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:History_of_the_United_States" title="Template talk:History of the United States"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:History_of_the_United_States&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>history of the Philippines from 1898 to 1946</b> describes the period of <b>American colonization of the Philippines.</b> It began with the outbreak of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish–American War">Spanish–American War</a> in April 1898, when the Philippines was still a colony of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_East_Indies" title="Spanish East Indies">Spanish East Indies</a>, and concluded when the United States <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Manila_(1946)" title="Treaty of Manila (1946)">formally recognised</a> the independence of the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Republic of the Philippines</a> on July 4, 1946.
</p><p>With the signing of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1898)" title="Treaty of Paris (1898)">Treaty of Paris</a> on December 10, 1898, Spain <a href="/wiki/Cession" title="Cession">ceded</a> the Philippines to the United States, thereby beginning the era of American colonization.<sup id="cite_ref-Avalon2008_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Avalon2008-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The interim <a href="/wiki/United_States_Military_Government_of_the_Philippine_Islands" title="United States Military Government of the Philippine Islands">U.S. military government of the Philippine Islands</a> experienced a period of great political turbulence, characterised by the <a href="/wiki/Philippine%E2%80%93American_War" title="Philippine–American War">Philippine–American War</a>.
</p><p>Beginning in 1901, the military government was replaced by a civilian government—the <a href="/wiki/Insular_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="Insular Government">Insular Government of the Philippine Islands</a>—with <a href="/wiki/William_Howard_Taft" title="William Howard Taft">William Howard Taft</a> serving as its first <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_the_Philippines#Insular_Government_(1901–1935)" title="Governor-General of the Philippines">Governor-General</a>. Also, from 1901 to 1906, there existed a series<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="Didn&#39;t most of these pre-date 1901? (August 2019)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> of <a href="/wiki/First_Philippine_Republic" title="First Philippine Republic">revolutionary governments</a> that lacked significant international and <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_recognition" title="Diplomatic recognition">diplomatic recognition</a>.
</p><p>Following the passage of the <a href="/wiki/Tydings%E2%80%93McDuffie_Act" title="Tydings–McDuffie Act">Philippine Independence Act</a> in 1934, a <a href="/wiki/1935_Philippine_presidential_election" title="1935 Philippine presidential election">Philippine presidential election</a> was held in 1935. <a href="/wiki/Manuel_L._Quezon" title="Manuel L. Quezon">Manuel L. Quezon</a> was elected and inaugurated second <a href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_the_Philippines" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Presidents of the Philippines">President of the Philippines</a> on November 15, 1935. The Insular Government was dissolved and the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_the_Philippines" title="Commonwealth of the Philippines">Commonwealth of the Philippines</a> was brought into existence. The Commonwealth of the Philippines was intended to be a transitional government in preparation for the country's full achievement of independence in 1946.<sup id="cite_ref-CJ2014_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CJ2014-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After the <a href="/wiki/Philippines_Campaign_(1941%E2%80%9342)" class="mw-redirect" title="Philippines Campaign (1941–42)">Japanese invasion</a> and subsequent <a href="/wiki/Japanese_occupation_of_the_Philippines" title="Japanese occupation of the Philippines">occupation of the Philippines</a> during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, the United States and Philippine Commonwealth military <a href="/wiki/Philippines_Campaign_(1944%E2%80%9345)" class="mw-redirect" title="Philippines Campaign (1944–45)">recaptured</a> the Philippines in 1945. According to the terms of the Philippine Independence Act,<sup id="cite_ref-CJ2014_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CJ2014-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> the United States formally recognised the independence of the Republic of the Philippines on July 4, 1946.
</p>

</div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_perspective">Historical perspective</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1898%E2%80%931946)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Historical perspective">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Revolution" title="Philippine Revolution">Philippine Revolution</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Emilio_Aguinaldo_(ca._1898).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Emilio_Aguinaldo_%28ca._1898%29.jpg/220px-Emilio_Aguinaldo_%28ca._1898%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="245" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/97/Emilio_Aguinaldo_%28ca._1898%29.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="303" data-file-height="338" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Emilio_Aguinaldo_(ca._1898).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President <a href="/wiki/Emilio_Aguinaldo" title="Emilio Aguinaldo">Emilio Aguinaldo</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Revolution" title="Philippine Revolution">Philippine Revolution</a> began in August 1896 and ended with the <a href="/wiki/Pact_of_Biak-na-Bato" title="Pact of Biak-na-Bato">Pact of Biak-na-Bato</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Ceasefire" title="Ceasefire">ceasefire</a> between the Spanish colonial Governor-General <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Primo_de_Rivera,_1st_Marquis_of_Estella" class="mw-redirect" title="Fernando Primo de Rivera, 1st Marquis of Estella">Fernando Primo de Rivera</a> and the revolutionary leader <a href="/wiki/Emilio_Aguinaldo" title="Emilio Aguinaldo">Emilio Aguinaldo</a> which was signed on December 15, 1897. The terms of the pact called for Aguinaldo and his <a href="/wiki/Militia" title="Militia">militia</a> to surrender. <a href="/wiki/Katipunan" title="Katipunan">Other revolutionary leaders</a> were given <a href="/wiki/Amnesty" title="Amnesty">amnesty</a> and a monetary <a href="/wiki/Indemnity" title="Indemnity">indemnity</a> by the Spanish government in return for which the rebel government agreed to go into exile in <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Aguinaldo1899-1_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aguinaldo1899-1-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Aguinaldo1899-2_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aguinaldo1899-2-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Kalaw1927p92-94_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kalaw1927p92-94-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Spanish.E2.80.93American_War_.281898.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish–American_War_(1898)">Spanish–American War (1898)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1898%E2%80%931946)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Spanish–American War (1898)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish–American War">Spanish–American War</a> and <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Revolution" title="Philippine Revolution">Philippine Revolution</a></div>
<p>The failure of Spain to engage in active social reforms in <a href="/wiki/Captaincy_General_of_Cuba" title="Captaincy General of Cuba">Cuba</a> as demanded by the United States government was the basic cause for the Spanish–American War. American attention was focused on the issue after the mysterious explosion that sank the American battleship <a href="/wiki/USS_Maine_(ACR-1)" title="USS Maine (ACR-1)"><i>Maine</i></a> on February 15, 1898 in <a href="/wiki/Havana_Harbor" title="Havana Harbor">Havana Harbor</a>. As public political pressure from the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_United_States_Democratic_Party" title="History of the United States Democratic Party">Democratic Party</a> and certain industrialists built up for war, the U.S. Congress forced the reluctant <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_United_States_Republican_Party" title="History of the United States Republican Party">Republican</a> President <a href="/wiki/William_McKinley" title="William McKinley">William McKinley</a> to issue an ultimatum to Spain on April 19, 1898. Spain found it had no diplomatic support in Europe, but nevertheless <a href="/wiki/Declaration_of_war" title="Declaration of war">declared war</a>; the U.S. followed on April 25 with its own declaration of war.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt" title="Theodore Roosevelt">Theodore Roosevelt</a>, who was at that time <a href="/wiki/Assistant_Secretary_of_the_Navy" title="Assistant Secretary of the Navy">Assistant Secretary of the Navy</a>, ordered Commodore <a href="/wiki/George_Dewey" title="George Dewey">George Dewey</a>, commanding the <a href="/wiki/Asiatic_Squadron" title="Asiatic Squadron">Asiatic Squadron</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a>: "Order the squadron ...to Hong Kong. Keep full of coal. In the event of declaration of war Spain, your duty will be to see that the Spanish squadron does not leave the Asiatic coast, and then offensive operations in Philippine Islands." Dewey's squadron departed on April 27 for the Philippines, reaching <a href="/wiki/Manila_Bay" title="Manila Bay">Manila Bay</a> on the evening of April 30.<sup id="cite_ref-Howland1921_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Howland1921-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Battle_of_Manila_Bay">Battle of Manila Bay</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1898%E2%80%931946)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Battle of Manila Bay">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Manila_Bay_by_W._G._Wood.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Battle_of_Manila_Bay_by_W._G._Wood.jpg/220px-Battle_of_Manila_Bay_by_W._G._Wood.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="122" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Battle_of_Manila_Bay_by_W._G._Wood.jpg/330px-Battle_of_Manila_Bay_by_W._G._Wood.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Battle_of_Manila_Bay_by_W._G._Wood.jpg/440px-Battle_of_Manila_Bay_by_W._G._Wood.jpg 2x" data-file-width="740" data-file-height="412" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Manila_Bay_by_W._G._Wood.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Manila_Bay" title="Battle of Manila Bay">Battle of Manila Bay</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Manila_Bay" title="Battle of Manila Bay">Battle of Manila Bay</a> took place on May 1, 1898. In a matter of hours, Commodore Dewey's Asiatic Squadron defeated the Spanish squadron under Admiral <a href="/wiki/Patricio_Montojo" class="mw-redirect" title="Patricio Montojo">Patricio Montojo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nhs-faq-BMB_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nhs-faq-BMB-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WTJ2003_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WTJ2003-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The U.S. squadron took control of the arsenal and navy yard at <a href="/wiki/Cavite" title="Cavite">Cavite</a>. Dewey cabled <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington</a>, stating that although he controlled Manila Bay, he needed 5,000 additional men to seize <a href="/wiki/Manila" title="Manila">Manila</a> itself.<sup id="cite_ref-nhs-faq-BMB_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nhs-faq-BMB-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="U.S._preparation_for_land-based_operations">U.S. preparation for land-based operations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1898%E2%80%931946)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: U.S. preparation for land-based operations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The unexpected rapidity and completeness of Dewey's victory in the first engagement of the war prompted the McKinley administration to make the decision to capture Manila from the Spanish. The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army" title="United States Army">United States Army</a> began to assemble the <a href="/wiki/Eighth_Army_Corps_(Spanish-American_War)" class="mw-redirect" title="Eighth Army Corps (Spanish-American War)">Eighth Army Corps</a>—a military unit which would consist of 10,844 soldiers under the command of Major General <a href="/wiki/Wesley_Merritt" title="Wesley Merritt">Wesley Merritt</a>—in preparation for deployment to the Philippines.<sup id="cite_ref-nhs-faq-BMB_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nhs-faq-BMB-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>While awaiting the arrival of troops from the Eighth Corps, Dewey dispatched the <a href="/wiki/Naval_cutter" class="mw-redirect" title="Naval cutter">cutter</a> <a href="/wiki/United_States_Revenue_Cutter_Service" title="United States Revenue Cutter Service">USRC</a> <a href="/wiki/USS_McCulloch_(1897)" title="USS McCulloch (1897)"><i>McCulloch</i></a> to Hong Kong to transport Aguinaldo back to the Philippines. 
</p><p>Aguinaldo arrived on May 19 and, after a brief meeting with Dewey, resumed revolutionary activities against the Spanish. On May 24, Aguinaldo issued a proclamation in which he assumed command of all Philippine forces and announced his intention to establish a <a href="/wiki/Dictatorship" title="Dictatorship">dictatorial government</a> with himself as dictator, saying that he would resign in favor of a duly elected president.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Public jubilation marked Aguinaldo's return. Many Filipino enlisted men <a href="/wiki/Desertion" title="Desertion">deserted</a> local Spanish army units to join Aguinaldo's command and the Philippine Revolution against Spain resumed. Soon, many cities such as <a href="/wiki/Imus" title="Imus">Imus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bacoor" title="Bacoor">Bacoor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Para%C3%B1aque" title="Parañaque">Parañaque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Las_Pi%C3%B1as" title="Las Piñas">Las Piñas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Morong,_Rizal" title="Morong, Rizal">Morong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Macabebe,_Pampanga" class="mw-redirect" title="Macabebe, Pampanga">Macabebe</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Fernando,_Pampanga" title="San Fernando, Pampanga">San Fernando</a>, as well as some entire <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_the_Philippines" title="Provinces of the Philippines">provinces</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Laguna_(province)" title="Laguna (province)">Laguna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Batangas" title="Batangas">Batangas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulacan" title="Bulacan">Bulacan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nueva_Ecija" title="Nueva Ecija">Nueva Ecija</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bataan" title="Bataan">Bataan</a>, Tayabas (now <a href="/wiki/Quezon" title="Quezon">Quezon</a>), and the <a href="/wiki/Ambos_Camarines" title="Ambos Camarines">Camarines</a> provinces, were liberated by the Filipinos and the port of Dalahican in Cavite was secured.<sup id="cite_ref-Agoncillo1990ch11pp192-194_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Agoncillo1990ch11pp192-194-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Thomas_M._Anderson_(1836%E2%88%921917).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Thomas_M._Anderson_%281836%E2%88%921917%29.jpg/170px-Thomas_M._Anderson_%281836%E2%88%921917%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="250" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Thomas_M._Anderson_%281836%E2%88%921917%29.jpg/255px-Thomas_M._Anderson_%281836%E2%88%921917%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Thomas_M._Anderson_%281836%E2%88%921917%29.jpg/340px-Thomas_M._Anderson_%281836%E2%88%921917%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="390" data-file-height="573" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Thomas_M._Anderson_(1836%E2%88%921917).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Thomas_M._Anderson" title="Thomas M. Anderson">Thomas M. Anderson</a></div></div></div>
<p>The first contingent of American troops arrived on 30 June under the command of Brigadier General <a href="/wiki/Thomas_M._Anderson" title="Thomas M. Anderson">Thomas McArthur Anderson</a>, commander of Eighth Corps' 2d Division (U.S. brigade and division numbers of the era were not unique throughout the army). General Anderson wrote to Aguinaldo, requesting his cooperation in military operations against the Spanish forces.<sup id="cite_ref-worcester1914ch3p57_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worcester1914ch3p57-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Aguinaldo responded, thanking General Anderson for his amicable sentiments, but saying nothing about military cooperation. General Anderson did not renew the request.<sup id="cite_ref-worcester1914ch3p57_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worcester1914ch3p57-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 2d Brigade, 2d Division, Eighth Corps arrived on July 17, under the command of Brigadier General <a href="/wiki/Francis_Vinton_Greene" title="Francis Vinton Greene">Francis V. Greene</a>. Major General Merritt (the <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief#United_States" title="Commander-in-chief">Commander in Chief</a> of the Philippine Expedition) and his staff arrived at Cavite on July 25. The 1st Brigade of the corps' 2d Division arrived on July 30, under the command of Brigadier General <a href="/wiki/Arthur_MacArthur,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Arthur MacArthur, Jr.">Arthur MacArthur</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Halstead1898ch10p95_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Halstead1898ch10p95-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philippine_declaration_of_independence">Philippine declaration of independence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1898%E2%80%931946)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Philippine declaration of independence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Revolutionary_Government_of_the_Philippines" class="mw-redirect" title="Revolutionary Government of the Philippines">Revolutionary Government of the Philippines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Declaration_of_Independence" title="Philippine Declaration of Independence">Philippine Declaration of Independence</a>, and <a href="/wiki/First_Philippine_Republic" title="First Philippine Republic">First Philippine Republic</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pic_geo_photos_-_ph%3Dcavite%3Dkawit%3Daguinaldo_shrine_-_front_view_-philippines--2015-0611--ls-_(1).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Pic_geo_photos_-_ph%3Dcavite%3Dkawit%3Daguinaldo_shrine_-_front_view_-philippines--2015-0611--ls-_%281%29.JPG/220px-Pic_geo_photos_-_ph%3Dcavite%3Dkawit%3Daguinaldo_shrine_-_front_view_-philippines--2015-0611--ls-_%281%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Pic_geo_photos_-_ph%3Dcavite%3Dkawit%3Daguinaldo_shrine_-_front_view_-philippines--2015-0611--ls-_%281%29.JPG/330px-Pic_geo_photos_-_ph%3Dcavite%3Dkawit%3Daguinaldo_shrine_-_front_view_-philippines--2015-0611--ls-_%281%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Pic_geo_photos_-_ph%3Dcavite%3Dkawit%3Daguinaldo_shrine_-_front_view_-philippines--2015-0611--ls-_%281%29.JPG/440px-Pic_geo_photos_-_ph%3Dcavite%3Dkawit%3Daguinaldo_shrine_-_front_view_-philippines--2015-0611--ls-_%281%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pic_geo_photos_-_ph%3Dcavite%3Dkawit%3Daguinaldo_shrine_-_front_view_-philippines--2015-0611--ls-_(1).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Aguinaldo_Shrine" title="Aguinaldo Shrine">Aguinaldo Shrine</a> where the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_the_Philippines" title="Flag of the Philippines">Flag of the Philippines</a> was waved declaring the Philippine independence from Spain</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:112px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marcela_de_Agoncillo.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Marcela_de_Agoncillo.png/110px-Marcela_de_Agoncillo.png" decoding="async" width="110" height="198" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Marcela_de_Agoncillo.png/165px-Marcela_de_Agoncillo.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/02/Marcela_de_Agoncillo.png 2x" data-file-width="174" data-file-height="313" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marcela_de_Agoncillo.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Marcela_Agoncillo" title="Marcela Agoncillo">Marcela Agoncillo</a></div></div></div>
<p>On 12 June 1898, Aguinaldo proclaimed the independence of the Philippines at <a href="/wiki/Aguinaldo_Shrine" title="Aguinaldo Shrine">his house</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kawit,_Cavite" title="Kawit, Cavite">Cavite El Viejo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pinas_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pinas-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ambrosio_Rianzares_Bautista" title="Ambrosio Rianzares Bautista">Ambrosio Rianzares Bautista</a> wrote the <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Declaration_of_Independence" title="Philippine Declaration of Independence">Philippine Declaration of Independence</a>, and read this document in Spanish that day at Aguinaldo's house.<sup id="cite_ref-Kalaw1927appA_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kalaw1927appA-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> On 18 June, Aguinaldo issued a decree formally establishing his dictatorial government.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> On June 23, Aguinaldo issued another decree, this time replacing the dictatorial government with a revolutionary government (and naming himself as President).<sup id="cite_ref-Kalaw1927appC_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kalaw1927appC-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>
Writing retrospectively in 1899, Aguinaldo claimed that an American naval officer had urged him to return to the Philippines to fight the Spanish and said "The United States is a great and rich nation and needs no colonies."<sup id="cite_ref-Aguinaldo1899-3_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aguinaldo1899-3-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Aguinaldo also wrote that after checking with Dewey by <a href="/wiki/Electrical_telegraph" title="Electrical telegraph">telegraph</a>, U.S. Consul <a href="/wiki/E._Spencer_Pratt" title="E. Spencer Pratt">E. Spencer Pratt</a> had assured him in <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>: </p><blockquote><p>"That the United States would at least recognize the independence of the Philippines under the protection of the United States Navy. The consul added that there was no necessity for entering into a formal written agreement because the word of the Admiral and of the United States Consul were in fact equivalent to the most solemn pledge that their verbal promises and assurance would be fulfilled to the letter and were not to be classed with Spanish promises or Spanish ideas of a man’s word of honour."<sup id="cite_ref-Aguinaldo1899-3_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aguinaldo1899-3-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> </p></blockquote><p>Aguinaldo received nothing in writing.
</p><div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marcela_Agoncillo_Ancestral_House.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Marcela_Agoncillo_Ancestral_House.JPG/220px-Marcela_Agoncillo_Ancestral_House.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Marcela_Agoncillo_Ancestral_House.JPG/330px-Marcela_Agoncillo_Ancestral_House.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Marcela_Agoncillo_Ancestral_House.JPG/440px-Marcela_Agoncillo_Ancestral_House.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2234" data-file-height="1674" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marcela_Agoncillo_Ancestral_House.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>House of <a href="/wiki/Marcela_Agoncillo" title="Marcela Agoncillo">Marcela Agoncillo</a> the mother of the Philippine flag</div></div></div>
<p>On April 28 Pratt wrote to <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_State" title="United States Secretary of State">United States Secretary of State</a> <a href="/wiki/William_R._Day" title="William R. Day">William R. Day</a>, explaining the details of his meeting with Aguinaldo: 
</p>
<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tbody><tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“
</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">"At this interview, after learning from General Aguinaldo the state of an object sought to be obtained by the present insurrectionary movement, which, though absent from the Philippines, he was still directing, I took it upon myself, whilst explaining that I had no authority to speak for the Government, to point out the danger of continuing independent action at this stage; and, having convinced him of the expediency of cooperating with our fleet, then at Hongkong, and obtained the assurance of his willingness to proceed thither and confer with Commodore Dewey to that end, should the latter so desire, I telegraphed the Commodore the same day as follows, through our consul-general at Hongkong:--<sup id="cite_ref-worcester1914ch2p19_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worcester1914ch2p19-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”
</td></tr>

</tbody></table>
<p>There was no mention in the cablegrams between Pratt and Dewey of independence or indeed of any conditions on which Aguinaldo was to cooperate, these details being left for future arrangement with Dewey. Pratt had intended to facilitate the occupation and administration of the Philippines, and also to prevent a possible conflict of action. In a communication written on July 28, Pratt made the following statement: 
</p>
<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tbody><tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“
</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">"I declined even to discuss with General Aguinaldo the question of the future policy of the United States with regard to the Philippines, that I held out no hopes to him of any kind, committed the government in no way whatever, and, in the course of our confidences, never acted upon the assumption that the Government would cooperate with him--General Aguinaldo--for the furtherance of any plans of his own, nor that, in accepting his said cooperation, it would consider itself pledged to recognize any political claims which he might put forward."<sup id="cite_ref-worcester1914ch2p21_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worcester1914ch2p21-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”
</td></tr>

</tbody></table>
<p>On June 16, Secretary Day cabled Consul Pratt: "Avoid unauthorized negotiations with the Philippine insurgents," and later on the same day:<sup id="cite_ref-Halstead1898ch28p311_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Halstead1898ch28p311-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> 
</p>
<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tbody><tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“
</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">The Department observes that you informed General Aguinaldo that you had no authority to speak for the United States; and, in the absence of the fuller report which you promise, it is assumed that you did not attempt to commit this Government to any alliance with the Philippine insurgents. To obtain the unconditional personal assistance of General Aguinaldo in the expedition to Manila was proper, if in so doing he was not induced to form hopes which it might not be practicable to gratify. This Government has known the Philippine insurgents only as discontented and rebellious subjects of Spain, and is not acquainted with their purposes. While their contest with that power has been a matter of public notoriety, they have neither asked nor received from this Government any recognition. The United States, in entering upon the occupation of the islands, as the result of its military operations in that quarter, will do so in the exercise of the rights which the state of war confers, and will expect from the inhabitants, without regard to their former attitude toward the Spanish Government, that obedience which will be lawfully due from them.
<p>If, in the course of your conferences with General Aguinaldo, you acted upon the assumption that this Government would co-operate with him for the furtherance of any plan of his own, or that, in accepting his co-operation, it would consider itself pledged to recognize any political claims which he may put forward, your action was unauthorized and can not be approved.
</p>
</td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”
</td></tr>

</tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Php_bill_5_back.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Php_bill_5_back.jpg/220px-Php_bill_5_back.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="88" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Php_bill_5_back.jpg/330px-Php_bill_5_back.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Php_bill_5_back.jpg/440px-Php_bill_5_back.jpg 2x" data-file-width="944" data-file-height="379" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Php_bill_5_back.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Independence_Day_(Philippines)" title="Independence Day (Philippines)">Independence Day</a> held in <a href="/wiki/Aguinaldo_Shrine" title="Aguinaldo Shrine">Aguinaldo Shrine</a> at the back of the old 5 peso bill</div></div></div><p>Filipino scholar <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maximo_Kalaw&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Maximo Kalaw (page does not exist)">Maximo Kalaw</a> wrote in 1927: "A few of the principal facts, however, seem quite clear. Aguinaldo was not made to understand that, in consideration of Filipino cooperation, the United States would extend its sovereignty over the Islands, and thus in place of the old Spanish master a new one would step in. The truth was that nobody at the time ever thought that the end of the war would result in the retention of the Philippines by the United States."<sup id="cite_ref-Kalaw1927p100_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kalaw1927p100-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tensions_between_U.S._and_revolutionary_forces">Tensions between U.S. and revolutionary forces</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1898%E2%80%931946)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Tensions between U.S. and revolutionary forces">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On July 9 General Anderson informed Major General <a href="/wiki/Henry_Clark_Corbin" title="Henry Clark Corbin">Henry Clark Corbin</a>, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Adjutants_General_of_the_U.S._Army" title="List of Adjutants General of the U.S. Army">Adjutant General of the U.S. Army</a>, that Aguinaldo "has declared himself Dictator and President, and is trying to take Manila without our assistance", opining that that would not be probable but, if done, would allow him to antagonize any U.S. attempt to establish a provisional government.<sup id="cite_ref-worcester1914ch3p60_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worcester1914ch3p60-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> On July 15, Aguinaldo issued three <a href="/wiki/Organic_law" title="Organic law">organic decrees</a> assuming civil authority of the Philippines.<sup id="cite_ref-worcester1914ch7p154_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worcester1914ch7p154-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FelipeAgoncillojf2144_02.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/FelipeAgoncillojf2144_02.JPG/220px-FelipeAgoncillojf2144_02.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/FelipeAgoncillojf2144_02.JPG/330px-FelipeAgoncillojf2144_02.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/FelipeAgoncillojf2144_02.JPG/440px-FelipeAgoncillojf2144_02.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FelipeAgoncillojf2144_02.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Felipe_Agoncillo" title="Felipe Agoncillo">Felipe Agoncillo</a> house</div></div></div>
<p>On July 18, General Anderson wrote that he suspected Aguinaldo to be secretly negotiating with the Spanish authorities.<sup id="cite_ref-worcester1914ch3p60_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worcester1914ch3p60-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> In a 21 July letter to the Adjutant General, General Anderson wrote that Aguinaldo had "put in operation an elaborate system of military government, under his assumed authority as Dictator, and has prohibited any supplies being given us, except by his order," and that Anderson had written to Aguinaldo that the requisitions on the country for necessary items must be filled, and that he must aid in having them filled.<sup id="cite_ref-worcester1914ch3p61_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worcester1914ch3p61-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>
On July 24, Aguinaldo wrote a letter to General Anderson in effect warning him not to disembark American troops in places conquered by the Filipinos from the Spaniards without first communicating in writing the places to be occupied and the object of the occupation. <a href="/wiki/Murat_Halstead" title="Murat Halstead">Murat Halstead</a>, official historian of the Philippine Expedition, writes that General Merritt remarked shortly after his arrival on 25 June, </p><blockquote><p>"As General Aguinaldo did not visit me on my arrival, nor offer his services as a subordinate military leader, and as my instructions from the President fully contemplated the occupation of the islands by the American land forces, and stated that 'the powers of the military occupant are absolute and supreme and immediately operate upon the political condition of the inhabitants,' I did not consider it wise to hold any direct communication with the insurgent leader until I should be in possession of the city of Manila, especially as I would not until then be in a position to issue a proclamation and enforce my authority, in the event that his pretensions should clash with my designs."<sup id="cite_ref-halstead1898ch10p97_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-halstead1898ch10p97-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote><p>U.S. commanders suspected that Aguinaldo and his forces were informing the Spanish of American movements. U.S. Army Major <a href="/wiki/John_R._M._Taylor" title="John R. M. Taylor">John R. M. Taylor</a> later wrote, after translating and analyzing insurgent documents,
</p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gregorio_del_Pilar_painting_at_PMA_Museum.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Gregorio_del_Pilar_painting_at_PMA_Museum.JPG/220px-Gregorio_del_Pilar_painting_at_PMA_Museum.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Gregorio_del_Pilar_painting_at_PMA_Museum.JPG/330px-Gregorio_del_Pilar_painting_at_PMA_Museum.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Gregorio_del_Pilar_painting_at_PMA_Museum.JPG/440px-Gregorio_del_Pilar_painting_at_PMA_Museum.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1504" data-file-height="2256" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gregorio_del_Pilar_painting_at_PMA_Museum.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>General <a href="/wiki/Gregorio_del_Pilar" title="Gregorio del Pilar">Gregorio del Pilar</a></div></div></div> 
<blockquote><p>"The officers of the United States Army who believed that the insurgents were informing the Spaniards of the American movements were right. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Manuel_Sastron_y_Pi%C3%B1ol&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Manuel Sastron y Piñol (page does not exist)">Sastrón</a> has printed a letter from <a href="/wiki/P%C3%ADo_del_Pilar" title="Pío del Pilar">Pío del Pilar</a>, dated July 30, to the Spanish officer commanding at <a href="/wiki/Santa_Ana,_Manila" title="Santa Ana, Manila">Santa Ana</a>, in which Pilar said that Aguinaldo had told him that the Americans would attack the Spanish lines on August 2 and advised that the Spaniards should not give way, but hold their positions. Pilar added, however, that if the Spaniards should fall back on the walled city and surrender Santa Ana to himself, he would hold it with his own men. Aguinaldo's information was correct, and on August 2 eight American soldiers were killed or wounded by the Spanish fire."<sup id="cite_ref-worcester1914ch3p63_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worcester1914ch3p63-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote><p>On the evening of August 12, on orders of General Merritt, General Anderson notified Aguinaldo to forbid the insurgents under his command from entering Manila. On 13 August, unaware of the peace protocol signing, U.S. forces assaulted and captured the Spanish positions in Manila. Insurgents made an independent attack of their own, as planned, which promptly led to trouble with the Americans. At 0800<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="(June 2019)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> that morning, Aguinaldo received a telegram from General Anderson, sternly warning him not to let his troops enter Manila without the consent of the American commander, who was situated on the south side of the <a href="/wiki/Pasig_River" title="Pasig River">Pasig River</a>. General Anderson's request was ignored, and Aguinaldo's forces crowded forward alongside the American forces until they directly confronted the Spanish troops. Although the Spanish were waving a <a href="/wiki/White_flag#Flag_of_temporary_truce_in_order_to_parley_(negotiate)" title="White flag">flag of truce</a>, the insurgents fired on the Spanish forces, provoking return fire. 19 American soldiers were killed, and 103 more were wounded in this action.<sup id="cite_ref-worcester1914ch3p55_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worcester1914ch3p55-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Halstead1898ch10p105_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Halstead1898ch10p105-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>General Anderson sent Aguinaldo a telegram, later that day, which read:
</p>
<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tbody><tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“
</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">Dated Ermita Headquarters 2nd Division 13 to Gen. Aguinaldo. Commanding Filipino Forces.--Manila, taken. Serious trouble threatened between our forces. Try and prevent it. Your troops should not force themselves in the city until we have received the full surrender then we will negotiate with you. -Anderson, commanding.
</td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”
</td></tr>

</tbody></table>
<p>Aguinaldo however demanded joint occupation of Manila. On August 13 Admiral Dewey and General Merritt informed their superiors of this and asked how far they might proceed in enforcing obedience in the matter.<sup id="cite_ref-worcester1914ch3p69_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worcester1914ch3p69-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>General Merritt received news of the August 12 peace protocol on August 16, three days after the surrender of Manila.<sup id="cite_ref-Halstead1898ch10p108_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Halstead1898ch10p108-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Admiral Dewey and General Merritt were informed by a telegram dated August 17 that the President of the United States had directed: 
</p>
<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tbody><tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“
</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">That there must be no joint occupation with the Insurgents. The United States in the possession of Manila city, Manila bay and harbor must preserve the peace and protect persons and property within the territory occupied by their military and naval forces. The insurgents and all others must recognize the military occupation and authority of the United States and the cessation of hostilities proclaimed by the President. Use whatever means in your judgment are necessary to this end.<sup id="cite_ref-worcester1914ch3p69_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worcester1914ch3p69-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”
</td></tr>

</tbody></table><p>
Insurgent forces were looting the portions of the city which they occupied, and were not confining their attacks to Spaniards, but were assaulting their own people and raiding the property of foreigners as well.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> U.S. commanders pressed Aguinaldo to withdraw his forces from Manila. Negotiations proceeded slowly and, on August 31, General <a href="/wiki/Elwell_Stephen_Otis" title="Elwell Stephen Otis">Elwell Otis</a> (General Merritt being unavailable) wrote, in a long letter to Aguinaldo: </p><blockquote><p>"... I am compelled by my instructions to direct that your armed forces evacuate the entire city of Manila, including its suburbs and defences, and that I shall be obliged to take action with that end in view within a very short space of time should you decline to comply with my Government's demands; and I hereby serve notice on you that unless your troops are withdrawn beyond the line of the city's defences before Thursday, the 15th instant, I shall be obliged to resort to forcible action, and that my Government will hold you responsible for any unfortunate consequences which may ensue."<sup id="cite_ref-worcester1914ch3p77_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worcester1914ch3p77-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> </p></blockquote><p>After further negotiation and exchanges of letters, Aguinaldo wrote on September 16: "On the evening of the 15th the armed insurgent organizations withdrew from the city and all of its suburbs, ..."<sup id="cite_ref-worcester1914ch3p79_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worcester1914ch3p79-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Peace_protocol_between_the_U.S._and_Spain">Peace protocol between the U.S. and Spain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1898%E2%80%931946)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Peace protocol between the U.S. and Spain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On August 12, 1898, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> reported that a <a href="/wiki/Armistice" title="Armistice">peace protocol</a> had been signed in Washington that afternoon between the U.S. and Spain, suspending hostilities between the two nations.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The full text of the protocol was not made public until November 5, but Article III read: "The United States will occupy and hold the City, Bay, and Harbor of Manila, pending the conclusion of a treaty of peace, which shall determine the control, disposition, and government of the Philippines."<sup id="cite_ref-Halstead1898ch15p177_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Halstead1898ch15p177-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> After conclusion of this agreement, U.S. President McKinley proclaimed a suspension of hostilities with Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Capture_of_Manila">Capture of Manila</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1898%E2%80%931946)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Capture of Manila">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Manila_(1898)" title="Battle of Manila (1898)">Battle of Manila (1898)</a></div>
<p>By June, U.S. and Filipino forces had taken control of most of the islands, except for the walled city of <a href="/wiki/Intramuros" title="Intramuros">Intramuros</a>. Admiral Dewey and General Merritt were able to work out a bloodless solution with acting Governor-General <a href="/wiki/Ferm%C3%ADn_J%C3%A1udenes" title="Fermín Jáudenes">Fermín Jáudenes</a>. The negotiating parties made a secret agreement to stage a mock battle in which the Spanish forces would be defeated by the American forces, but the Filipino forces would not be allowed to enter the city. This plan minimized the risk of unnecessary casualties on all sides, while the Spanish would also avoid the shame of possibly having to surrender Intramuros to the Filipino forces.<sup id="cite_ref-karnow1990p123_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-karnow1990p123-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> On the eve of the mock battle, General Anderson telegraphed Aguinaldo, "Do not let your troops enter Manila without the permission of the American commander. On this side of the Pasig River you will be under fire".<sup id="cite_ref-agoncillo1990p196_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-agoncillo1990p196-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On August 13, with American commanders unaware that a ceasefire had already been signed between Spain and the U.S. on the previous day, American forces captured the city of Manila from the Spanish in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Manila_(1898)" title="Battle of Manila (1898)">Battle of Manila</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-U.S._Library_of_Congress_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-U.S._Library_of_Congress-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> The battle started when Dewey's ships bombarded <a href="/wiki/Fort_San_Antonio_Abad" title="Fort San Antonio Abad">Fort San Antonio Abad</a>, a decrepit structure on the <a href="/wiki/Malate,_Manila" title="Malate, Manila">southern outskirts of Manila</a>, and the virtually impregnable walls of Intramuros. In accordance with the plan, the Spanish forces withdrew while U.S. forces advanced. Once a sufficient show of battle had been made, Dewey hoisted the signal "D.W.H.B." (meaning "Do you surrender?),<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> whereupon the Spanish hoisted a white flag and Manila was formally surrendered to U.S. forces.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:270px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Antonio_luna_small.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/74/Antonio_luna_small.jpg" decoding="async" width="268" height="400" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="268" data-file-height="400" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Antonio_luna_small.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>General <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Luna" title="Antonio Luna">Antonio Luna</a></div></div></div>
<p>This battle marked the end of Filipino-American collaboration, as the American action of preventing Filipino forces from entering the captured city of Manila was deeply resented by the Filipinos. This later led to the Philippine–American War,<sup id="cite_ref-lac126_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lac126-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> which would prove to be more deadly and costly than the Spanish–American War.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="U.S._military_government">U.S. military government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1898%E2%80%931946)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: U.S. military government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On August 14, 1898, two days after the capture of Manila, the U.S. established a <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_the_Philippines#United_States_Military_Government_(1898–1901)" title="Governor-General of the Philippines">military government</a> in the Philippines, with General <a href="/wiki/Wesley_Merritt" title="Wesley Merritt">Merritt</a> acting as military governor.<sup id="cite_ref-Halstead1898ch11pp110-112_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Halstead1898ch11pp110-112-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> During military rule (1898–1902), the U.S. military commander governed the Philippines under the authority of the U.S. president as <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-Chief" class="mw-redirect" title="Commander-in-Chief">Commander-in-Chief</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Armed_Forces" title="United States Armed Forces">United States Armed Forces</a>. After the appointment of a <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_the_Philippines#Insular_Government_(1901–1935)" title="Governor-General of the Philippines">civil Governor-General</a>, the procedure developed that as parts of the country were pacified and placed firmly under American control, responsibility for the area would be passed to the civilian.
</p><p>General Merritt was succeeded by General <a href="/wiki/Elwell_Stephen_Otis" title="Elwell Stephen Otis">Otis</a> as military governor, who in turn was succeeded by General <a href="/wiki/Arthur_MacArthur,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Arthur MacArthur, Jr.">MacArthur</a>. Major General <a href="/wiki/Adna_Chaffee" title="Adna Chaffee">Adna Chaffee</a> was the final military governor. The position of military governor was abolished in July 1902, after which the civil Governor-General became the sole executive authority in the Philippines.<sup id="cite_ref-End_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-End-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AmnestyProc_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AmnestyProc-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Under the military government, an American-style school system was introduced, initially with soldiers as teachers; civil and criminal courts were reestablished, including a supreme court;<sup id="cite_ref-Otis1899_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Otis1899-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> and local governments were established in towns and provinces. The first local election was conducted by General Harold W. Lawton on May 7, 1899, in <a href="/wiki/Baliuag,_Bulacan" title="Baliuag, Bulacan">Baliuag, Bulacan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Zaide1994ch21p279_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zaide1994ch21p279-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="U.S._and_insurgents_clash">U.S. and insurgents clash</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1898%E2%80%931946)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: U.S. and insurgents clash">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Philippine%E2%80%93American_War" title="Philippine–American War">Philippine–American War</a></div>
<p>In a clash at Cavite between United States soldiers and insurgents on August 25, 1898, George Hudson of the Utah regiment was killed, Corporal William Anderson was mortally wounded, and four troopers of the Fourth Cavalry were slightly wounded.<sup id="cite_ref-Halstead1898ch28p315_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Halstead1898ch28p315-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-taylor1907p19_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-taylor1907p19-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> This provoked General Anderson to send Aguinaldo a letter saying, "In order to avoid the very serious misfortune of an encounter between our troops, I demand your immediate withdrawal with your guard from Cavite. One of my men has been killed and three wounded by your people. This is positive and does not admit of explanation or delay."<sup id="cite_ref-taylor1907p19_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-taylor1907p19-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Internal insurgent communications reported that the Americans were drunk at the time. Halstead writes that Aguinaldo expressed his regret and promised to punish the offenders.<sup id="cite_ref-Halstead1898ch28p315_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Halstead1898ch28p315-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> In internal insurgent communications, <a href="/wiki/Apolinario_Mabini" title="Apolinario Mabini">Apolinario Mabini</a> initially proposed to investigate and punish any offenders identified. Aguinaldo modified this, ordering, "... say that he was not killed by your soldiers, but by them themselves [the Americans] since they were drunk according to your telegram".<sup id="cite_ref-taylor1907p20_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-taylor1907p20-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> An insurgent officer in Cavite at the time reported on his record of services that he: "took part in the movement against the Americans on the afternoon of the 24th of August, under the orders of the commander of the troops and the adjutant of the post."<sup id="cite_ref-worcester1914ch4p83_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worcester1914ch4p83-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Philippine_elections.2C_Malolos_Congress.2C_Constitutional_government"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Philippine_elections,_Malolos_Congress,_Constitutional_government">Philippine elections, Malolos Congress, Constitutional government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1898%E2%80%931946)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Philippine elections, Malolos Congress, Constitutional government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/1898_Philippine_Malolos_Congress_election" class="mw-redirect" title="1898 Philippine Malolos Congress election">Elections</a> were held by the Revolutionary Government between June and September 10, resulting in Emilio Aguinaldo being seated as President in the seating of a legislature known as the <a href="/wiki/Revolutionary_Government_of_the_Philippines" class="mw-redirect" title="Revolutionary Government of the Philippines">Malolos Congress</a>. In a session between September 15 and November 13, 1898, the <a href="/wiki/Malolos_Constitution" title="Malolos Constitution">Malolos Constitution</a> was adopted. It was promulgated on January 21, 1899,
creating the <a href="/wiki/First_Philippine_Republic" title="First Philippine Republic">First Philippine Republic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Spanish.E2.80.93American_War_ends"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish–American_War_ends">Spanish–American War ends</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1898%E2%80%931946)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Spanish–American War ends">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1898)" title="Treaty of Paris (1898)">Treaty of Paris (1898)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Felipe_Agoncillo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Felipe_Agoncillo.jpg/220px-Felipe_Agoncillo.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="272" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Felipe_Agoncillo.jpg/330px-Felipe_Agoncillo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e1/Felipe_Agoncillo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="357" data-file-height="442" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Felipe_Agoncillo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Felipe_Agoncillo" title="Felipe Agoncillo">Felipe Agoncillo</a> was the Filipino lawyer representative to the negotiations in <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a> that led to the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1898)" title="Treaty of Paris (1898)">Treaty of Paris (1898)</a>, ending the <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish–American War">Spanish–American War</a> and giving him the title of "<i>outstanding first Filipino diplomat</i>."</div></div></div><p>
Article V of the peace protocol signed on August 12 had mandated negotiations to conclude a treaty of peace to begin in Paris not later than October 1, 1898.<sup id="cite_ref-Halstead1898ch15pp176-178_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Halstead1898ch15pp176-178-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> President McKinley sent a five-man commission, initially instructed to demand no more than <a href="/wiki/Luzon" title="Luzon">Luzon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">Guam</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>; which would have provided a limited U.S. empire of pinpoint colonies to support a global fleet and provide communication links.<sup id="cite_ref-miller1984p20_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-miller1984p20-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> In Paris, the commission was besieged with advice, particularly from American generals and European diplomats, to demand the entire Philippine archipelago.<sup id="cite_ref-miller1984p20_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-miller1984p20-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> The unanimous recommendation was that "it would certainly be cheaper and more humane to take the entire Philippines than to keep only part of it."<sup id="cite_ref-miller1984pp20-21_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-miller1984pp20-21-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> On October 28, 1898, McKinley wired the commission that "cessation of Luzon alone, leaving the rest of the islands subject to Spanish rule, or to be the subject of future contention, cannot be justified on political, commercial, or humanitarian grounds. The cessation must be the whole archipeligo or none. The latter is wholly inadmissible, and the former must therefore be required."<sup id="cite_ref-miller1984p24_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-miller1984p24-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> The Spanish negotiators were furious over the "immodist demands of a conqueror", but their wounded pride was assuaged by an offer of twenty million dollars for "Spanish improvements" to the islands. The Spaniards capitulated, and on December 10, 1898, the U.S. and Spain signed the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1898)" title="Treaty of Paris (1898)">Treaty of Paris</a>, formally ending the Spanish–American War. In Article III, Spain ceded the Philippine archipelago to the United States, as follows: "Spain cedes to the United States the archipelago known as the Philippine Islands, and comprehending the islands lying within the following line: [... geographic description elided ...]. The United States will pay to Spain the sum of twenty million dollars ($20,000,000) within three months after the exchange of the ratifications of the present treaty."<sup id="cite_ref-Kalaw1927:430-445_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kalaw1927:430-445-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup></p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:McKinleyPhilippinesCartoon.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/McKinleyPhilippinesCartoon.jpg/220px-McKinleyPhilippinesCartoon.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="264" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/McKinleyPhilippinesCartoon.jpg/330px-McKinleyPhilippinesCartoon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a4/McKinleyPhilippinesCartoon.jpg 2x" data-file-width="432" data-file-height="519" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:McKinleyPhilippinesCartoon.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1898 US political cartoon. U.S. President <a href="/wiki/William_McKinley" title="William McKinley">William McKinley</a> is shown holding the Philippines, depicted as a native child, as the world looks on. The implied options for McKinley are to keep the Philippines, or give it back to Spain, which the cartoon compares to throwing a child off a cliff.</div></div></div>
<p>In the U.S., there was a movement for Philippine independence; some said that the U.S. had no right to a land where many of the people wanted self-government. In 1898 <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Carnegie" title="Andrew Carnegie">Andrew Carnegie</a>, an industrialist and steel magnate, offered to pay the U.S. government $20 million to give the Philippines its independence.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On November 7, 1900, Spain and the U.S. signed the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Washington_(1900)" title="Treaty of Washington (1900)">Treaty of Washington</a>, clarifying that the territories relinquished by Spain to the United States included any and all islands belonging to the Philippine Archipelago, but lying outside the lines described in the Treaty of Paris. That treaty explicitly named the islands of <a href="/wiki/Mapun,_Tawi-Tawi" class="mw-redirect" title="Mapun, Tawi-Tawi">Cagayan Sulu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sibutu,_Tawi-Tawi" class="mw-redirect" title="Sibutu, Tawi-Tawi">Sibutu</a> and their dependencies as among the relinquished territories.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Benevolent_assimilation">Benevolent assimilation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1898%E2%80%931946)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Benevolent assimilation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Benevolent_assimilation" title="Benevolent assimilation">Benevolent assimilation</a></div><p>U.S. President McKinley's December 21, 1898 proclamation of Benevolent Assimilation was announced in the Philippines on January 4, 1899. Referring to the Treaty of Paris, it said that as a result of the victories of American arms, the future control, disposition, and government of the Philippine Islands are ceded to the United States. It enjoined the military commander (General Otis) to make known to the inhabitants of the Philippine Islands that in succeeding to the sovereignty of Spain, the authority of the United States is to be exerted for the securing of the persons and property of the people of the islands and for the confirmation of all their private rights and relations. It specified that it will be the duty of the commander of the forces of occupation to announce and proclaim in the most public manner that we come, not as invaders or conquerors, but as friends, to protect the natives in their homes, in their employments, and in their personal and religious rights.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> On January 6, 1899, General Otis was quoted in <i>The New York Times</i> as expressing himself as convinced that the U.S. government intends to seek the establishment of a liberal government, in which the people will be as fully represented as the maintenance of law and order will permit, susceptible of development, on lines of increased representation, and the bestowal of increased powers, into a government as free and independent as is enjoyed by the most favored provinces in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><h2><span id="Philippine.E2.80.93American_War_.281899.E2.80.931902.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Philippine–American_War_(1899–1902)">Philippine–American War (1899–1902)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1898%E2%80%931946)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Philippine–American War (1899–1902)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Philippine%E2%80%93American_War" title="Philippine–American War">Philippine–American War</a></div><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Moro_Rebellion" title="Moro Rebellion">Moro Rebellion</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tensions_escalate">Tensions escalate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1898%E2%80%931946)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Tensions escalate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gregorio_del_Pilar_and_his_troops,_around_1898.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Gregorio_del_Pilar_and_his_troops%2C_around_1898.jpg/220px-Gregorio_del_Pilar_and_his_troops%2C_around_1898.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Gregorio_del_Pilar_and_his_troops%2C_around_1898.jpg/330px-Gregorio_del_Pilar_and_his_troops%2C_around_1898.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Gregorio_del_Pilar_and_his_troops%2C_around_1898.jpg/440px-Gregorio_del_Pilar_and_his_troops%2C_around_1898.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="325" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gregorio_del_Pilar_and_his_troops,_around_1898.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Gregorio_del_Pilar" title="Gregorio del Pilar">Gregorio del Pilar</a> and his troops in1898</div></div></div>
<p>The Spanish had yielded <a href="/wiki/Iloilo" title="Iloilo">Iloilo</a> to the insurgents in 1898 for the purpose of troubling the Americans. On January 1, 1899, news had come to Washington from Manila that American forces which had been sent to Iloilo under the command of General Marcus Miller had been confronted by 6,000 armed Filipinos, who refused them permission to land.<sup id="cite_ref-Halstead1898ch28p316_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Halstead1898ch28p316-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-miller1984p51_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-miller1984p51-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> A Filipino official styling himself Presidente Lopez of the Federal Government of the Visayas informed Miller that "foreign troops" would not be landed "without express orders from the central government of Luzon"<sup id="cite_ref-miller1984p51_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-miller1984p51-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> On December 21, 1898, President McKinley issued a <a href="/wiki/Benevolent_assimilation" title="Benevolent assimilation">Proclamation of Benevolent Assimilation</a>. General Otis delayed its publication until January 4, 1899, then publishing an amended version edited so as not to convey the meanings of the terms "sovereignty", "protection", and "right of cessation" which were present in the unabridged version.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Unknown to Otis, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_War" title="United States Department of War">War Department</a> had also sent an enciphered copy of the Benevolent Assimilation proclamation to General Marcus Miller in Iloilo for informational purposes. Miller assumed that it was for distribution and, unaware that a politically <a href="/wiki/Expurgation" title="Expurgation">bowdlerized</a> version had been sent to Aguinaldo, published it in both Spanish and Tagalog translations which eventually made their way to Aguinaldo.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> Even before Aguinaldo received the unaltered version and observed the changes in the copy he had received from Otis, he was upset that Otis had altered his own title to "Military Governor of the Philippines" from "... <i>in</i> the Philippines." Aguinaldo did not miss the significance of the alteration, which Otis had made without authorization from Washington.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:356px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Quingua.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Battle_of_Quingua.jpg/354px-Battle_of_Quingua.jpg" decoding="async" width="354" height="253" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Battle_of_Quingua.jpg/531px-Battle_of_Quingua.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Battle_of_Quingua.jpg/708px-Battle_of_Quingua.jpg 2x" data-file-width="8227" data-file-height="5882" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Quingua.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Battle of Quingua, April 23, 1899 <a href="/wiki/Philippine%E2%80%93American_War" title="Philippine–American War">Philippine–American War</a></div></div></div>
<p>On January 5, Aguinaldo issued a counter-proclamation summarizing what he saw as American violations of the ethics of friendship, particularly as regards the events in Iloilo. The proclamation concluded as follows:
</p>
<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tbody><tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“
</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">Such procedures, so foreign to the dictates of culture and the usages observed by civilized nations, gave me the right to act without observing the usual rules of intercourse. Nevertheless, in order to be correct to the end, I sent to General Otis commissioners charged to solicit him to desist from his rash enterprise, but they were not listened to.
<p>My government can not remain indifferent in view of such a violent and aggressive seizure of a portion of its territory by a nation which arrogated to itself the title champion of oppressed nations. Thus it is that my government is disposed to open hostilities if the American troops attempt to take forcible possession of the Visayan Islands. I denounce these acts before the world, in order that the conscience of mankind may pronounce its infallable verdict as to who are the true oppressors of nations and the tormentors of human kind.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
</td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”
</td></tr>

</tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:363px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_before_Caloocan,_02-10-1899.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Battle_before_Caloocan%2C_02-10-1899.jpg/361px-Battle_before_Caloocan%2C_02-10-1899.jpg" decoding="async" width="361" height="236" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Battle_before_Caloocan%2C_02-10-1899.jpg/542px-Battle_before_Caloocan%2C_02-10-1899.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Battle_before_Caloocan%2C_02-10-1899.jpg/722px-Battle_before_Caloocan%2C_02-10-1899.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2544" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_before_Caloocan,_02-10-1899.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Battle before Caloocan</div></div></div>
