<p>After some copies of that proclamation had been distributed, Aguinaldo ordered the recall of undistributed copies and issued another proclamation, which was published the same day in <i>El Heraldo de la Revolucion</i>, the official newspaper of the Philippine Republic. There, he said partly,
</p>
<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tbody><tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“
</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">As in General Otis's proclamation he alluded to some instructions edited by His Excellency the President of the United States, referring to the administration of the matters in the Philippine Islands, I in the name of God, the root and fountain of all justice, and that of all the right which has been visibly granted to me to direct my dear brothers in the difficult work of our regeneration, protest most solemnly against this intrusion of the United States Government on the sovereignty of these islands.
<p>I equally protest in the name of the Filipino people against the said intrusion, because as they have granted their vote of confidence appointing me president of the nation, although I don't consider that I deserve such, therefore I consider it my duty to defend to death its liberty and independence.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
</td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”
</td></tr>

</tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:315px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LeadingtheTroops-SantaCruz-0.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/LeadingtheTroops-SantaCruz-0.jpg/313px-LeadingtheTroops-SantaCruz-0.jpg" decoding="async" width="313" height="226" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/LeadingtheTroops-SantaCruz-0.jpg/470px-LeadingtheTroops-SantaCruz-0.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/LeadingtheTroops-SantaCruz-0.jpg/626px-LeadingtheTroops-SantaCruz-0.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1234" data-file-height="892" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LeadingtheTroops-SantaCruz-0.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Battle of Santa Cruz</div></div></div>
<p>Otis, taking these two proclamations as a call to arms, strengthened American observation posts and alerted his troops. In the tense atmosphere, some 40,000 Filipinos fled Manila within a period of 15 days.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Meanwhile, <a href="/wiki/Felipe_Agoncillo" title="Felipe Agoncillo">Felipe Agoncillo</a>, who had been commissioned by the Philippine Revolutionary Government as Minister Plenipotentiary to negotiate treaties with foreign governments, and who had unsuccessfully sought to be seated at the negotiations between the U.S. and Spain in Paris, was now in Washington. On January 6, he filed a request for an interview with the President to discuss affairs in the Philippines. The next day the government officials were surprised to learn that messages to General Otis to deal mildly with the rebels and not to force a conflict had become known to Agoncillo, and cabled by him to Aguinaldo. At the same time came Aguinaldo's protest against General Otis signing himself "Military Governor of the Philippines."<sup id="cite_ref-Halstead1898ch28p316_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Halstead1898ch28p316-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On January 8, Agoncillo gave out this statement:<sup id="cite_ref-Halstead1898ch28p316_68-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Halstead1898ch28p316-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tbody><tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“
</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">In my opinion the Filipino people, whom I represent, will never consent to become a colony dependency of the United States. The soldiers of the Filipino army have pledged their lives that they will not lay down their arms until General Aguinaldo tells them to do so, and they will keep that pledge, I feel confident.
</td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”
</td></tr>

</tbody></table>
<p>The Filipino committees in London, Paris and Madrid about this time telegraphed to President McKinley as follows:
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:369px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Americans_guarding_Pasig_River_bridge,_1898.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Americans_guarding_Pasig_River_bridge%2C_1898.jpg/367px-Americans_guarding_Pasig_River_bridge%2C_1898.jpg" decoding="async" width="367" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Americans_guarding_Pasig_River_bridge%2C_1898.jpg/551px-Americans_guarding_Pasig_River_bridge%2C_1898.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Americans_guarding_Pasig_River_bridge%2C_1898.jpg/734px-Americans_guarding_Pasig_River_bridge%2C_1898.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1122" data-file-height="672" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Americans_guarding_Pasig_River_bridge,_1898.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>American troops guarding the bridge over the River Pasig</div></div></div>
<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tbody><tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“
</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">We protest against the disembarkation of American troops at Iloilo. The treaty of peace still unratified, the American claim to sovereignty is premature. Pray reconsider the resolution regarding Iloilo. Filipinos wish for the friendship of America and abhor militarism and deceit.<sup id="cite_ref-Halstead1898ch28p316_68-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Halstead1898ch28p316-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”
</td></tr>

</tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:318px;"><a href="/wiki/File:YoungsScouts.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/YoungsScouts.jpg/316px-YoungsScouts.jpg" decoding="async" width="316" height="261" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/YoungsScouts.jpg/474px-YoungsScouts.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/YoungsScouts.jpg/632px-YoungsScouts.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="1980" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:YoungsScouts.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Young's Scouts, including Marcus W. Robertson(2nd from right, front row squating), Richard Moses Longfellow(4th from right, front row squating), Medal of Honor recipients. Picture taken in Philippines.</div></div></div>
<p>On January 8, Aguinaldo received the following message from <a href="/wiki/Teodoro_Sandiko" title="Teodoro Sandiko">Teodoro Sandiko</a>:
</p>
<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tbody><tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“
</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">To the President of the Revolutionary Government, Malolos, from Sandico, Manila. 8 Jan., 1899, 9.40 p.m..: In consequence of the order of General Rios to his officers, as soon as the Filipino attack begins the Americans should be driven into the Intramuros district and the walled city should be set on fire. Pipi.<sup id="cite_ref-taylor1907p39_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-taylor1907p39-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”
</td></tr>

</tbody></table>
<p><i>The New York Times</i> reported on January 8, that two Americans who had been guarding a waterboat in Iloilo had been attacked, one fatally, and that insurgents were threatening to destroy the business section of the city by fire; and on January 10 that a peaceful solution to the Iloilo issues may result but that Aguinaldo had issued a proclamation threatening to drive the Americans from the islands.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Harpersweeklyapr241899.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Harpersweeklyapr241899.png/290px-Harpersweeklyapr241899.png" decoding="async" width="290" height="372" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Harpersweeklyapr241899.png/435px-Harpersweeklyapr241899.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/70/Harpersweeklyapr241899.png 2x" data-file-width="562" data-file-height="720" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Harpersweeklyapr241899.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Attack on the barracks of Company C of the 13th Minnesota Volunteers by Filipino forces during the Tondo Fire in Manila, 1899</div></div></div>
<p>By January 10, insurgents were ready to assume the offensive, but desired, if possible, to provoke the Americans into firing the first shot. They made no secret of their desire for conflict, but increased their hostile demonstrations and pushed their lines forward into forbidden territory. Their attitude is well illustrated by the following extract from a telegram sent by Colonel Cailles to Aguinaldo on January 10, 1899:<sup id="cite_ref-worcester1914ch4p93_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worcester1914ch4p93-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tbody><tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“
</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">Most urgent. An American interpreter has come to tell me to withdraw our forces in Maytubig fifty paces. I shall not draw back a step, and in place of withdrawing, I shall advance a little farther. He brings a letter from his general, in which he speaks to me as a friend. I said that from the day I knew that Maquinley (McKinley) opposed our independence I did not want any dealings with any American. War, war, is what we want. The Americans after this speech went off pale.
</td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”
</td></tr>

</tbody></table>
<p>Aguinaldo approved the hostile attitude of Cailles, for there is a reply in his handwriting which reads:<sup id="cite_ref-worcester1914ch4p93_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worcester1914ch4p93-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tbody><tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“
</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">I approve and applaud what you have done with the Americans, and zeal and valour always, also my beloved officers and soldiers there. I believe that they are playing us until the arrival of their reinforcements, but I shall send an ultimatum and remain always on the alert.--E. A. Jan. 10, 1899.
</td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”
</td></tr>

</tbody></table>
<p>On 31 January 1899, The Minister of Interior of the revolutionary First Philippine Republic, Teodoro Sandiko, signed a decree saying that President Aguinaldo had directed that all idle lands be planted to provide food for the people, in view of impending war with the Americans.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Outbreak_of_general_hostilities">Outbreak of general hostilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1898%E2%80%931946)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Outbreak of general hostilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Manila_(1899)" title="Battle of Manila (1899)">Battle of Manila (1899)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Philippines,_Manila,_1899-_U.S._soldiers_and_insurrecto_prisoners_at_the_cathedral,_Walled_City_LCCN2005691616.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Philippines%2C_Manila%2C_1899-_U.S._soldiers_and_insurrecto_prisoners_at_the_cathedral%2C_Walled_City_LCCN2005691616.jpg/290px-Philippines%2C_Manila%2C_1899-_U.S._soldiers_and_insurrecto_prisoners_at_the_cathedral%2C_Walled_City_LCCN2005691616.jpg" decoding="async" width="290" height="201" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Philippines%2C_Manila%2C_1899-_U.S._soldiers_and_insurrecto_prisoners_at_the_cathedral%2C_Walled_City_LCCN2005691616.jpg/435px-Philippines%2C_Manila%2C_1899-_U.S._soldiers_and_insurrecto_prisoners_at_the_cathedral%2C_Walled_City_LCCN2005691616.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Philippines%2C_Manila%2C_1899-_U.S._soldiers_and_insurrecto_prisoners_at_the_cathedral%2C_Walled_City_LCCN2005691616.jpg/580px-Philippines%2C_Manila%2C_1899-_U.S._soldiers_and_insurrecto_prisoners_at_the_cathedral%2C_Walled_City_LCCN2005691616.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="1066" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Philippines,_Manila,_1899-_U.S._soldiers_and_insurrecto_prisoners_at_the_cathedral,_Walled_City_LCCN2005691616.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Philippines, Manila, 1899- U.S. soldiers and insurrecto prisoners</div></div></div>
<p>Worcester writes that General Otis' account of the opening of active hostilities was as follows: 
</p>
<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tbody><tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“
</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">"On the night of February 2 they sent in a strong detachment to draw the fire of our outposts, which took up a position immediately in front and within a few yards of the same. The outpost was strengthened by a few of our men, who silently bore their taunts and abuse the entire night. This was reported to me by General MacArthur, whom I directed to communicate with the officer in command of the insurgent troops concerned. His prepared letter was shown me and approved, and the reply received was all that could be desired. However, the agreement was ignored by the insurgents and on the evening of February 4 another demonstration was made on one of our small outposts, which occupied a retired position at least 150 yards within the line which had been mutually agreed upon, an insurgent approaching the picket and refusing to halt or answer when challenged. The result was that our picket discharged his piece, when the insurgent troops near Santa Mesa opened a spirited fire on our troops there stationed.
<p>"The insurgents had thus succeeded in drawing the fire of a small outpost, which they had evidently labored with all their ingenuity to accomplish, in order to justify in some way their premeditated attack. It is not believed that the chief insurgent leaders wished to open hostilities at this time, as they were not completely prepared to assume the initiative. They desired two or three days more to perfect their arrangements, but the zeal of their army brought on the crisis which anticipated their premeditated action. They could not have delayed long, however, for it was their object to force an issue before American troops, then en route, could arrive in Manila."
</p><p>Thus began the Insurgent attack, so long and so carefully planned for. We learn from the Insurgent records that the shot of the American sentry missed its mark. There was no reason why it should have provoked a hot return fire, but it did.
</p><p>The result of the ensuing combat was not at all what the Insurgents had anticipated. The Americans did not drive very well. It was but a short time before they themselves were routed and driven from their positions.
</p><p>Aguinaldo of course promptly advanced the claim that his troops had been wantonly attacked. The plain fact is that the Insurgent patrol in question deliberately drew the fire of the American sentry, and this was just as much an act of war as was the firing of the shot. Whether the patrol was acting under proper orders from higher authority is not definitely known.<sup id="cite_ref-worcester1914ch4p96_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worcester1914ch4p96-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
</td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”
</td></tr>

</tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:274px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Emilio_Aguinaldo_boarding_USS_Vicksburg.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Emilio_Aguinaldo_boarding_USS_Vicksburg.jpg/272px-Emilio_Aguinaldo_boarding_USS_Vicksburg.jpg" decoding="async" width="272" height="244" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Emilio_Aguinaldo_boarding_USS_Vicksburg.jpg/408px-Emilio_Aguinaldo_boarding_USS_Vicksburg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9f/Emilio_Aguinaldo_boarding_USS_Vicksburg.jpg 2x" data-file-width="541" data-file-height="485" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Emilio_Aguinaldo_boarding_USS_Vicksburg.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Surrendered President Aguinaldo boards the U.S.S Vicksburg, 1900.</div></div></div>
<p>Other sources name the two specific U.S. soldiers involved in the first exchange of fire as Privates William Grayson and Orville Miller of the Nebraska Volunteers.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Subsequent to the conclusion of the war, after analyzing captured insurgent papers, Major Major J. R. M. Taylor wrote, in part,
</p>
<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tbody><tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“
</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">An attack on the United States forces was planned which should annihilate the little army in Manila, and delegations were appointed to secure the interference of foreign powers. The protecting cloak of pretense of friendliness to the United States was to be kept up until the last. While commissioners were appointed to negotiate with General Otis, secret societies were organized in Manila pledged to obey orders of the most barbarous character to kill and burn. The attack from without and the attack from within was to be on a set day and hour. The strained situation could not last. The spark was applied, either inadvertently or by design, on the 4th of February by an insurgent, willfully transgressing upon what, by their own admission, was within the agreed limits of the holding of the American troops. Hostilities resulted and the war was an accomplished fact.<sup id="cite_ref-taylor1907p5_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-taylor1907p5-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”
</td></tr>

</tbody></table>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="War">War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1898%E2%80%931946)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:335px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Filipino_casualties_on_the_first_day_of_war.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Filipino_casualties_on_the_first_day_of_war.jpg/333px-Filipino_casualties_on_the_first_day_of_war.jpg" decoding="async" width="333" height="268" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Filipino_casualties_on_the_first_day_of_war.jpg/500px-Filipino_casualties_on_the_first_day_of_war.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Filipino_casualties_on_the_first_day_of_war.jpg/666px-Filipino_casualties_on_the_first_day_of_war.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2944" data-file-height="2370" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Filipino_casualties_on_the_first_day_of_war.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Filipino casualties</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:331px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aguinaldo%27s_quarters_in_Manila_after_capture.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Aguinaldo%27s_quarters_in_Manila_after_capture.JPG/329px-Aguinaldo%27s_quarters_in_Manila_after_capture.JPG" decoding="async" width="329" height="228" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Aguinaldo%27s_quarters_in_Manila_after_capture.JPG/494px-Aguinaldo%27s_quarters_in_Manila_after_capture.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Aguinaldo%27s_quarters_in_Manila_after_capture.JPG/658px-Aguinaldo%27s_quarters_in_Manila_after_capture.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2003" data-file-height="1386" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aguinaldo%27s_quarters_in_Manila_after_capture.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Emilio Aguinaldo's quarters in Manila following his capture by the Americans.</div></div></div>
<p>On February 4, Aguinaldo declared "That peace and friendly relations with the Americans be broken and that the latter be treated as enemies, within the limits prescribed by the laws of war."<sup id="cite_ref-Halstead1898ch28p318_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Halstead1898ch28p318-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> On June 2, 1899, the <a href="/wiki/Malolos_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Malolos Republic">Malolos Congress</a> enacted and ratified a declaration of war on the United States, which was publicly proclaimed on that same day by <a href="/wiki/Pedro_A._Paterno" class="mw-redirect" title="Pedro A. Paterno">Pedro Paterno</a>, President of the Assembly.<sup id="cite_ref-Kalaw1927:199-200_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kalaw1927:199-200-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As before when fighting the Spanish, the Filipino rebels did not do well in the field. Aguinaldo and his provisional government escaped after the capture of Malolos on March 31, 1899 and were driven into northern Luzon. Peace feelers from members of Aguinaldo's cabinet failed in May when the American commander, General Ewell Otis, demanded an unconditional surrender. In 1901, Aguinaldo was captured and swore allegiance to the United States, marking one end to the war.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_Philippine_Commission">First Philippine Commission</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1898%E2%80%931946)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: First Philippine Commission">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Schurman_Commission" title="Schurman Commission">Schurman Commission</a></div><p>
President McKinley had appointed a five-person group headed by <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Gould_Schurman" title="Jacob Gould Schurman">Dr. Jacob Schurman</a>, president of <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University" title="Cornell University">Cornell University</a>, on January 20, 1899, to investigate conditions in the islands and make recommendations. </p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Philippine-American_War.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Philippine-American_War.png/200px-Philippine-American_War.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="271" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Philippine-American_War.png/300px-Philippine-American_War.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Philippine-American_War.png/399px-Philippine-American_War.png 2x" data-file-width="709" data-file-height="962" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Philippine-American_War.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1899 political cartoon by <a href="/wiki/Winsor_McCay" title="Winsor McCay">Winsor McCay</a>. Uncle Sam (representing the United States), gets entangled with rope around a tree labelled "Imperialism" while trying to subdue a bucking colt or mule labeled "Philippines" while a figure representing Spain walks off over the horizon carrying a bag labeled "$20,000,000".</div></div></div><p> The three civilian members of the <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Commission" title="Philippine Commission">Philippine Commission</a> arrived in Manila on March 4, 1899, a month after the Battle of Manila which had begun armed conflict between U.S. and revolutionary Filipino forces. The commission published a proclamation containing assurances that the U.S. "... is anxious to establish in the Philippine Islands an enlightened system of government under which the Philippine people may enjoy the largest measure of home rule and the amplest liberty."
</p><p>After meetings in April with revolutionary representatives, the commission requested authorization from McKinley to offer a specific plan. McKinley authorized an offer of a government consisting of "a Governor-General appointed by the President; cabinet appointed by the Governor-General; [and] a general advisory council elected by the people."<sup id="cite_ref-golay1997p49_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-golay1997p49-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> The Revolutionary Congress voted unanimously to cease fighting and accept peace and, on May 8, the revolutionary cabinet headed by Apolinario Mabini was replaced by a new "peace" cabinet headed by Pedro Paterno. At this point, General <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Luna" title="Antonio Luna">Antonio Luna</a> arrested Paterno and most of his cabinet, returning Mabini and his cabinet to power. After this, the commission concluded that "... The Filipinos are wholly unprepared for independence ... there being no Philippine nation, but only a collection of different peoples."<sup id="cite_ref-golay1997pp50-51_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-golay1997pp50-51-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the report that they issued to the president the following year, the commissioners acknowledged Filipino aspirations for independence; they declared, however, that the Philippines was not ready for it.<sup id="cite_ref-worcester1914ch9p199_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worcester1914ch9p199-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tbody><tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“
</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">On November 2, 1899, The commission issued a preliminary report containing the following statement: <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886047036">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Should our power by any fatality be withdrawn, the commission believe that the government of the Philippines would speedily lapse into anarchy, which would excuse, if it did not necessitate, the intervention of other powers and the eventual division of the islands among them. Only through American occupation, therefore, is the idea of a free, self-governing, and united Philippine commonwealth at all conceivable. And the indispensable need from the Filipino point of view of maintaining American sovereignty over the archipelago is recognized by all intelligent Filipinos and even by those insurgents who desire an American protectorate. The latter, it is true, would take the revenues and leave us the responsibilities. Nevertheless, they recognize the indubitable fact that the Filipinos cannot stand alone. Thus the welfare of the Filipinos coincides with the dictates of national honour in forbidding our abandonment of the archipelago. We cannot from any point of view escape the responsibilities of government which our sovereignty entails; and the commission is strongly persuaded that the performance of our national duty will prove the greatest blessing to the peoples of the Philippine Islands.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
</td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”
</td></tr>

</tbody></table>
<p> Specific recommendations included the establishment of civilian government as rapidly as possible (the American chief executive in the islands at that time was the military governor), including establishment of a <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">bicameral legislature</a>, autonomous governments on the provincial and municipal levels, and a system of free public elementary schools.<sup id="cite_ref-Seekins1993US-Rule_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Seekins1993US-Rule-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_Philippine_Commission">Second Philippine Commission</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1898%E2%80%931946)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Second Philippine Commission">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Taft_Commission" title="Taft Commission">Taft Commission</a></div>
<p>The Second Philippine Commission (the Taft Commission), appointed by McKinley on March 16, 1900, and headed by <a href="/wiki/William_Howard_Taft" title="William Howard Taft">William Howard Taft</a>, was granted legislative as well as limited executive powers.<sup id="cite_ref-Kalaw1927appFp453_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kalaw1927appFp453-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> On September 1, the Taft Commission began to exercise legislative functions.<sup id="cite_ref-Zaide1994ch24p280_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zaide1994ch24p280-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> Between September 1900 and August 1902, it issued 499 laws, established a judicial system, including a supreme court, drew up a legal code, and organized a civil service.<sup id="cite_ref-chronphil_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chronphil-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> The 1901 municipal code provided for popularly elected presidents, vice presidents, and councilors to serve on municipal boards. The municipal board members were responsible for collecting taxes, maintaining municipal properties, and undertaking necessary construction projects; they also elected provincial governors.<sup id="cite_ref-Seekins1993US-Rule_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Seekins1993US-Rule-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Establishment_of_civil_government">Establishment of civil government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1898%E2%80%931946)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Establishment of civil government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:344px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Taft_Addressing_First_Philippine_Assembly_1907.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Taft_Addressing_First_Philippine_Assembly_1907.jpg/342px-Taft_Addressing_First_Philippine_Assembly_1907.jpg" decoding="async" width="342" height="185" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Taft_Addressing_First_Philippine_Assembly_1907.jpg/513px-Taft_Addressing_First_Philippine_Assembly_1907.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/65/Taft_Addressing_First_Philippine_Assembly_1907.jpg 2x" data-file-width="608" data-file-height="329" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Taft_Addressing_First_Philippine_Assembly_1907.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Governor General <a href="/wiki/William_Howard_Taft" title="William Howard Taft">William Howard Taft</a> addressing the audience at the <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Assembly" title="Philippine Assembly">Philippine Assembly</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Manila_Grand_Opera_House" title="Manila Grand Opera House">Manila Grand Opera House</a></div></div></div><p>On March 3, 1901 the U.S. Congress passed the Army Appropriation Act containing (along with the <a href="/wiki/Platt_Amendment" title="Platt Amendment">Platt Amendment</a> on Cuba) the <a href="/wiki/Spooner_Amendment" class="mw-redirect" title="Spooner Amendment">Spooner Amendment</a> which provided the President with legislative authority to establish of a civil government in the Philippines.<sup id="cite_ref-Piedad-Pugay_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Piedad-Pugay-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> Up until this time, the President been administering the Philippines by virtue of his war powers.<sup id="cite_ref-Jernegan2009pp57-58_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jernegan2009pp57-58-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> On July 1, 1901, civil government was inaugurated with William H. Taft as the Civil Governor. Later, on February 3, 1903, the U.S. Congress would change the title of <i>Civil Governor</i> to <i>Governor-General</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Zaide1994ch21p281_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zaide1994ch21p281-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A highly centralized public school system was installed in 1901, using English as the medium of instruction. This created a heavy shortage of teachers, and the Philippine Commission authorized the Secretary of Public Instruction to bring to the Philippines 600 teachers from the U.S.A. — the so-called <a href="/wiki/Thomasites" title="Thomasites">Thomasites</a>. Free primary instruction that trained the people for the duties of citizenship and avocation was enforced by the Taft Commission per instructions of President McKinley.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> Also, the Catholic Church was disestablished, and a considerable amount of church land was purchased and redistributed.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Official_end_to_the_war">Official end to the war</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1898%E2%80%931946)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Official end to the war">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Organic_Act_(1902)" title="Philippine Organic Act (1902)">Philippine Organic Act</a> of July 1902 approved, ratified, and confirmed McKinley's Executive Order establishing the Philippine Commission, and also stipulated that the bicameral <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Legislature" title="Philippine Legislature">Philippine Legislature</a> would be established composed of an elected lower house, the <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Assembly" title="Philippine Assembly">Philippine Assembly</a> and the appointed Philippine Commission as the upper house. The act also provided for extending the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Bill_of_Rights" title="United States Bill of Rights">United States Bill of Rights</a> to the Philippines.<sup id="cite_ref-Seekins1993US-Rule_91-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Seekins1993US-Rule-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On July 2, 1902 the Secretary of War telegraphed that the insurrection against the sovereign authority of the U.S. having come to an end, and provincial civil governments having been established, the office of Military Governor was terminated.<sup id="cite_ref-AmnestyProc_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AmnestyProc-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> On July 4, <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt" title="Theodore Roosevelt">Theodore Roosevelt</a>, who had succeeded to the U.S. Presidency after the assassination of President McKinley on September 5, 1901 proclaimed a full and complete pardon and amnesty to all persons in the Philippine archipelago who had participated in the conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-AmnestyProc_51-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AmnestyProc-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-worcester1914ch9p180_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worcester1914ch9p180-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On April 9, 2002, Philippine President <a href="/wiki/Gloria_Macapagal_Arroyo" title="Gloria Macapagal Arroyo">Gloria Macapagal Arroyo</a> proclaimed that the Philippine–American War had ended on April 16, 1902 with the surrender of General <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Malvar" title="Miguel Malvar">Miguel Malvar</a>, and declared the centennial anniversary of that date as a national working holiday and as a special non-working holiday in the Province of <a href="/wiki/Batangas" title="Batangas">Batangas</a> and in the Cities of <a href="/wiki/Batangas_City" title="Batangas City">Batangas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lipa,_Batangas" title="Lipa, Batangas">Lipa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tanauan,_Batangas" title="Tanauan, Batangas">Tanaun</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-1902_hostilities">Post-1902 hostilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1898%E2%80%931946)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Post-1902 hostilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Some sources have suggested that the war unofficially continued for nearly a decade, since bands of guerrillas, quasi-religious armed groups and other resistance groups continued to roam the countryside, still clashing with American Army or Philippine Constabulary patrols. American troops and the <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Constabulary" title="Philippine Constabulary">Philippine Constabulary</a> continued hostilities against such resistance groups until 1913.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> Some historians consider these unofficial extensions to be part of the war.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="US_colonization:_the_.22Insular_Government.22_.281901.E2.80.931935.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="US_colonization:_the_&quot;Insular_Government&quot;_(1901–1935)">US colonization: the "Insular Government" (1901–1935)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1898%E2%80%931946)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: US colonization: the &quot;Insular Government&quot; (1901–1935)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Insular_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="Insular Government">Insular Government</a></div><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:354px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Calle_Sebastian_Calle_Hidalgo_Manila.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Calle_Sebastian_Calle_Hidalgo_Manila.jpg/352px-Calle_Sebastian_Calle_Hidalgo_Manila.jpg" decoding="async" width="352" height="215" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Calle_Sebastian_Calle_Hidalgo_Manila.jpg/528px-Calle_Sebastian_Calle_Hidalgo_Manila.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Calle_Sebastian_Calle_Hidalgo_Manila.jpg/704px-Calle_Sebastian_Calle_Hidalgo_Manila.jpg 2x" data-file-width="736" data-file-height="450" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Calle_Sebastian_Calle_Hidalgo_Manila.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Tranvia in Manila during the American Era with <a href="/wiki/Bahay_na_Bato" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahay na Bato">Bahay na Bato</a> houses. Calle San Sebastian, present-day Felix Hidalgo St.</div></div></div><p>The 1902 Philippine Organic Act was a constitution for the Insular Government, as the U.S. colonial administration was known. This was a form of territorial government that reported to the <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Insular_Affairs" title="Bureau of Insular Affairs">Bureau of Insular Affairs</a>. The act provided for a Governor-General appointed by the U.S. president and an elected lower house, the <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Assembly" title="Philippine Assembly">Philippine Assembly</a>. It also disestablished the Catholic Church as the state religion. The United States government, in an effort to resolve the status of the friars, negotiated with the Vatican. The church agreed to sell the friars' estates and promised gradual substitution of Filipino and other non-Spanish priests for the friars. It refused, however, to withdraw the religious orders from the islands immediately, partly to avoid offending Spain. In 1904 the administration bought for $7.2 million the major part of the friars' holdings, amounting to some 166,000 hectares (410,000 acres), of which one-half was in the vicinity of Manila. The land was eventually resold to Filipinos, some of them tenants but the majority of them estate owners.<sup id="cite_ref-Seekins1993US-Rule_91-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Seekins1993US-Rule-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup></p><div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:371px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Plaza_Moraga_old_Manila.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Plaza_Moraga_old_Manila.jpg/369px-Plaza_Moraga_old_Manila.jpg" decoding="async" width="369" height="250" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Plaza_Moraga_old_Manila.jpg/554px-Plaza_Moraga_old_Manila.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/69/Plaza_Moraga_old_Manila.jpg 2x" data-file-width="695" data-file-height="470" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Plaza_Moraga_old_Manila.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Manila, known as the <a href="/wiki/Paris_of_the_East" title="Paris of the East">Paris of the Asia</a> was pushed forward even more by <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Burnham" title="Daniel Burnham">Daniel Burnham</a> the Manila Urban planner. Plaza Goiti, present-day <a href="/wiki/Plaza_Lacson" title="Plaza Lacson">Plaza Lacson</a></div></div></div><p>In socio-economic terms, the Philippines made solid progress in this period. Foreign trade had amounted to 62 million pesos in 1895, 13% of which was with the United States. By 1920, it had increased to 601 million pesos, 66% of which was with the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> A health care system was established which, by 1930, reduced the <a href="/wiki/Mortality_rate" title="Mortality rate">mortality rate</a> from all causes, including various <a href="/wiki/Tropical_disease" title="Tropical disease">tropical diseases</a>, to a level similar to that of the United States itself. The practices of <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slavery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Piracy" title="Piracy">piracy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Headhunting" title="Headhunting">headhunting</a> were suppressed but not entirely extinguished.</p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:337px;"><a href="/wiki/File:El_Hogar_building_Manila.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/El_Hogar_building_Manila.jpg/335px-El_Hogar_building_Manila.jpg" decoding="async" width="335" height="218" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/El_Hogar_building_Manila.jpg/503px-El_Hogar_building_Manila.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/El_Hogar_building_Manila.jpg/670px-El_Hogar_building_Manila.jpg 2x" data-file-width="885" data-file-height="576" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:El_Hogar_building_Manila.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Economy rose as reflected to the great edifices of the cities. <a href="/wiki/El_Hogar_Filipino_Building" title="El Hogar Filipino Building">El Hogar Filipino Building</a></div></div></div><p>Two years after completion and publication of a census, a general election was conducted for the choice of delegates to a popular assembly. An elected Philippine Assembly was convened in 1907 as the lower house of a <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">bicameral legislature</a>, with the Philippine Commission as the upper house.
</p><p>Every year from 1907 the Philippine Assembly and later the Philippine Legislature passed resolutions expressing the Filipino desire for independence.
</p><p>
Philippine nationalists led by <a href="/wiki/Manuel_L._Quezon" title="Manuel L. Quezon">Manuel L. Quezon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sergio_Osme%C3%B1a" title="Sergio Osmeña">Sergio Osmeña</a> enthusiastically endorsed the draft Jones Bill of 1912, which provided for Philippine independence after eight years, but later changed their views, opting for a bill which focused less on time than on the conditions of independence. The nationalists demanded complete and absolute independence to be guaranteed by the United States, since they feared that too-rapid independence from American rule without such guarantees might cause the Philippines to fall into Japanese hands. The Jones Bill was rewritten and passed Congress in 1916 with a later date of independence.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup></p><div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:364px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Plaza_Moraga_Manila_Philippines.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Plaza_Moraga_Manila_Philippines.jpg/362px-Plaza_Moraga_Manila_Philippines.jpg" decoding="async" width="362" height="198" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Plaza_Moraga_Manila_Philippines.jpg/543px-Plaza_Moraga_Manila_Philippines.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Plaza_Moraga_Manila_Philippines.jpg/724px-Plaza_Moraga_Manila_Philippines.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1236" data-file-height="677" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Plaza_Moraga_Manila_Philippines.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Busy street of early American-era Manila. <a href="/wiki/Plaza_Moraga" title="Plaza Moraga">Plaza Moraga</a></div></div></div><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:389px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Manila_American_era.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Manila_American_era.jpg/387px-Manila_American_era.jpg" decoding="async" width="387" height="263" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Manila_American_era.jpg/581px-Manila_American_era.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Manila_American_era.jpg/774px-Manila_American_era.jpg 2x" data-file-width="925" data-file-height="628" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Manila_American_era.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View of Binondo from <a href="/wiki/Jones_Bridge" title="Jones Bridge">Jones Bridge</a></div></div></div>
<p>The law, officially the <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Autonomy_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="Philippine Autonomy Act">Philippine Autonomy Act</a> but popularly known as the <a href="/wiki/Jones_Law_(Philippines)" title="Jones Law (Philippines)">Jones Law</a>, served as the new organic act (or constitution) for the Philippines. Its preamble stated that the eventual independence of the Philippines would be American policy, subject to the establishment of a stable government. The law maintained the Governor-General of the Philippines, appointed by the President of the United States, but established a bicameral Philippine Legislature to replace the elected Philippine Assembly (lower house); it replaced the appointive Philippine Commission (upper house) with an elected senate.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:361px;"><a href="/wiki/File:La_Opinion_Manila.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/La_Opinion_Manila.jpg/359px-La_Opinion_Manila.jpg" decoding="async" width="359" height="265" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/La_Opinion_Manila.jpg/539px-La_Opinion_Manila.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/La_Opinion_Manila.jpg/718px-La_Opinion_Manila.jpg 2x" data-file-width="777" data-file-height="573" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:La_Opinion_Manila.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Americans and Filipinos choose to preserve Spanish-era buildings for historical, tourism and urban purposes.</div></div></div><p>
The Filipinos suspended their independence campaign during the First World War and supported the United States against Germany. After the war they resumed their independence drive with great vigor.<sup id="cite_ref-Zaide1994ch24pp312_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zaide1994ch24pp312-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> On March 17, 1919, the Philippine Legislature passed a "Declaration of Purposes", which stated the inflexible desire of the Filipino people to be free and sovereign. A Commission of Independence was created to study ways and means of attaining liberation ideal. This commission recommended the sending of an independence mission to the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-Zaide1994ch24pp312-313_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zaide1994ch24pp312-313-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> The "Declaration of Purposes" referred to the Jones Law as a veritable pact, or covenant, between the American and Filipino peoples whereby the United States promised to recognize the independence of the Philippines as soon as a stable government should be established. U.S. Governor-General of the Philippines <a href="/wiki/Francis_Burton_Harrison" title="Francis Burton Harrison">Francis Burton Harrison</a> had concurred in the report of the Philippine legislature as to a stable government.</p><div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:331px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jones-Bridge-skyview-with-Post-Office-1930s.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Jones-Bridge-skyview-with-Post-Office-1930s.jpg/329px-Jones-Bridge-skyview-with-Post-Office-1930s.jpg" decoding="async" width="329" height="199" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Jones-Bridge-skyview-with-Post-Office-1930s.jpg/494px-Jones-Bridge-skyview-with-Post-Office-1930s.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Jones-Bridge-skyview-with-Post-Office-1930s.jpg/658px-Jones-Bridge-skyview-with-Post-Office-1930s.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="969" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jones-Bridge-skyview-with-Post-Office-1930s.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>With Manila's Filipino Hispanic roots, <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Burnham" title="Daniel Burnham">Daniel Burnham</a> developed the Urban planning of Manila through the <a href="/wiki/City_Beautiful_movement" title="City Beautiful movement">City Beautiful Movement</a>; Neo-Classical architecture of Paris through Manila's Government buildings, <a href="/wiki/Grand_Canal_(Venice)" title="Grand Canal (Venice)">Canals</a> of <a href="/wiki/Venice" title="Venice">Venice</a> through the Esteros of Manila, Sunset view of <a href="/wiki/Naples" title="Naples">Naples</a> through <a href="/wiki/Manila_Bay" title="Manila Bay">Manila Bay</a> and Winding River of Paris through the <a href="/wiki/Pasig_River" title="Pasig River">Pasig River</a>. A fine example of the Burnham plan is the <a href="/wiki/Manila_Central_Post_Office" title="Manila Central Post Office">Manila Central Post Office</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jones_Bridge" title="Jones Bridge">Jones Bridge</a> <a href="/wiki/Manila" title="Manila">Manila</a> circa 1930s.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:317px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Central_facade_of_the_Legislative_Building.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Central_facade_of_the_Legislative_Building.jpg/315px-Central_facade_of_the_Legislative_Building.jpg" decoding="async" width="315" height="273" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Central_facade_of_the_Legislative_Building.jpg/473px-Central_facade_of_the_Legislative_Building.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Central_facade_of_the_Legislative_Building.jpg/630px-Central_facade_of_the_Legislative_Building.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="833" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Central_facade_of_the_Legislative_Building.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The central façade of the Legislative Building</div></div></div>
<p>The Philippine legislature funded an independence mission to the U.S. in 1919. The mission departed Manila on February 28 and met in the U.S. with and presented their case to <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_War" title="United States Secretary of War">Secretary of War</a> <a href="/wiki/Newton_D._Baker" title="Newton D. Baker">Newton D. Baker</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Zaide1994ch24p313_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zaide1994ch24p313-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Woodrow_Wilson" title="Woodrow Wilson">Woodrow Wilson</a>, in his 1921 farewell message to Congress, certified that the Filipino people had performed the condition imposed on them as a prerequisite to independence, declaring that, this having been done, the duty of the U.S. is to grant Philippine independence.<sup id="cite_ref-Kalaw1921pp144-146_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kalaw1921pp144-146-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican Party</a> then controlled Congress and the recommendation of the outgoing <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a> president was not heeded.<sup id="cite_ref-Zaide1994ch24p313_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zaide1994ch24p313-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After the first independence mission, public funding of such missions was ruled illegal. Subsequent independence missions in 1922, 1923, 1930, 1931 1932, and two missions in 1933 were funded by voluntary contributions. Numerous independence bills were submitted to the U.S. Congress, which passed the Hare-Hawes-Cutting Bill on December 30, 1932. U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Hoover" title="Herbert Hoover">Herbert Hoover</a> vetoed the bill on January 13, 1933. Congress overrode the veto on January 17, and the <a href="/wiki/Hare%E2%80%93Hawes%E2%80%93Cutting_Act" title="Hare–Hawes–Cutting Act">Hare–Hawes–Cutting Act</a> became U.S. law. The law promised Philippine independence after 10 years, but reserved several military and naval bases for the United States, as well as imposing tariffs and quotas on Philippine exports. The law also required the <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Senate" class="mw-redirect" title="Philippine Senate">Philippine Senate</a> to ratify the law. <a href="/wiki/Manuel_L._Quezon" title="Manuel L. Quezon">Manuel L. Quezon</a> urged the Philippine Senate to reject the bill, which it did. Quezon himself led the twelfth independence mission to Washington to secure a better independence act. The result was the <a href="/wiki/Tydings%E2%80%93McDuffie_Act" title="Tydings–McDuffie Act">Tydings–McDuffie Act</a> of 1934 which was very similar to the Hare-Hawes-Cutting Act except in minor details. The Tydings-McDuffie Act was ratified by the Philippine Senate. The law provided for the granting of Philippine independence by 1946.<sup id="cite_ref-Zaide1994ch24pp314-315_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zaide1994ch24pp314-315-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Tydings–McDuffie Act provided for the drafting and guidelines of a <a href="/wiki/1935_Constitution_of_the_Philippines" class="mw-redirect" title="1935 Constitution of the Philippines">Constitution</a>, for a 10-year <i>"transitional period"</i> as the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_the_Philippines" title="Commonwealth of the Philippines">Commonwealth of the Philippines</a> before the granting of <a href="/wiki/Republic_Day_(Philippines)" title="Republic Day (Philippines)">Philippine independence</a>. On May 5, 1934, the Philippines legislature passed an act setting the election of convention delegates. Governor-General <a href="/wiki/Frank_Murphy" title="Frank Murphy">Frank Murphy</a> designated July 10 as the election date, and the convention held its inaugural session on July 30. The completed draft constitution was approved by the convention on February 8, 1935, approved by U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin Roosevelt</a> on March 23, and ratified by popular vote on May 14. The first election under the constitution was held on September 17, and on November 15, 1935, the Commonwealth was put into place.<sup id="cite_ref-Zaide1994ch24pp315-319_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zaide1994ch24pp315-319-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Philippine_Commonwealth_.281935.E2.80.931946.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Philippine_Commonwealth_(1935–1946)">Philippine Commonwealth (1935–1946)<span id="Commonwealth_era_(1935–1946)"></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1898%E2%80%931946)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Philippine Commonwealth (1935–1946)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:151px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Quezon.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Quezon.jpg/149px-Quezon.jpg" decoding="async" width="149" height="242" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Quezon.jpg/224px-Quezon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Quezon.jpg/298px-Quezon.jpg 2x" data-file-width="416" data-file-height="675" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Quezon.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Manuel_L._Quezon" title="Manuel L. Quezon">Manuel Quezon y Molina</a>, once the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Senate_of_the_Philippines" title="President of the Senate of the Philippines">President of the Senate of the Philippines</a> (and the first to hold that office), was elected to become the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Philippines" title="President of the Philippines">President of the Philippines</a> during the Commonwealth era of American colonization and occupation</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_the_Philippines" title="Commonwealth of the Philippines">Commonwealth of the Philippines</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:391px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Plaza_Moraga_Manila.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Plaza_Moraga_Manila.jpg/389px-Plaza_Moraga_Manila.jpg" decoding="async" width="389" height="221" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Plaza_Moraga_Manila.jpg/584px-Plaza_Moraga_Manila.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Plaza_Moraga_Manila.jpg/778px-Plaza_Moraga_Manila.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1304" data-file-height="740" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Plaza_Moraga_Manila.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Manila before the war</div></div></div>
<p>It was planned that the period 1935–1946 would be devoted to the final adjustments required for a peaceful transition to full independence, a great latitude in autonomy being granted in the meantime. Instead there was war with Japan.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On May 14, 1935, an election to fill the newly created office of President of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_the_Philippines" title="Commonwealth of the Philippines">Commonwealth of the Philippines</a> was won by <a href="/wiki/Manuel_L._Quezon" title="Manuel L. Quezon">Manuel L. Quezon</a> (<a href="/wiki/Nacionalista_Party" title="Nacionalista Party">Nacionalista Party</a>), and a Filipino government was formed on the basis of principles superficially similar to the <a href="/wiki/U.S._constitution" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. constitution">U.S. Constitution</a>. The Commonwealth as established in 1935 featured a very strong executive, a unicameral <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_the_Philippines" title="National Assembly of the Philippines">national assembly</a>, and a supreme court composed entirely of Filipinos for the first time since 1901. The new government embarked on an ambitious agenda of establishing the basis for national defense, greater control over the economy, reforms in education, improvement of transport, the colonization of the island of Mindanao, and the promotion of local capital and industrialization. The Commonwealth however, was also faced with agrarian unrest, an uncertain diplomatic and military situation in South East Asia, and uncertainty about the level of United States commitment to the future Republic of the Philippines.
</p><p>In 1939–40, the Philippine Constitution was amended to restore a bicameral Congress, and permit the reelection of President Quezon, previously restricted to a single, six-year term.
</p><p>During the Commonwealth years, Philippines sent one elected <a href="/wiki/Resident_Commissioners_from_the_Philippines" class="mw-redirect" title="Resident Commissioners from the Philippines">Resident Commissioner</a> to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">United States House of Representatives</a>, as <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> currently does today.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Japanese_troops_on_Bataan,_Philippine_Islands,_circa_1942._Captured_Japanese_photograph._-_NARA_-_531353.tif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Japanese_troops_on_Bataan%2C_Philippine_Islands%2C_circa_1942._Captured_Japanese_photograph._-_NARA_-_531353.tif/lossy-page1-200px-Japanese_troops_on_Bataan%2C_Philippine_Islands%2C_circa_1942._Captured_Japanese_photograph._-_NARA_-_531353.tif.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="300" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Japanese_troops_on_Bataan%2C_Philippine_Islands%2C_circa_1942._Captured_Japanese_photograph._-_NARA_-_531353.tif/lossy-page1-300px-Japanese_troops_on_Bataan%2C_Philippine_Islands%2C_circa_1942._Captured_Japanese_photograph._-_NARA_-_531353.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Japanese_troops_on_Bataan%2C_Philippine_Islands%2C_circa_1942._Captured_Japanese_photograph._-_NARA_-_531353.tif/lossy-page1-400px-Japanese_troops_on_Bataan%2C_Philippine_Islands%2C_circa_1942._Captured_Japanese_photograph._-_NARA_-_531353.tif.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2003" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Japanese_troops_on_Bataan,_Philippine_Islands,_circa_1942._Captured_Japanese_photograph._-_NARA_-_531353.tif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Japanese troops on Bataan, Philippine Islands, circa 1942. Captured Japanese photograph. - NARA - 531353</div></div></div>
<h2><span id="Japanese_occupation_and_World_War_II_.281941.E2.80.931945.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Japanese_occupation_and_World_War_II_(1941–1945)">Japanese occupation and World War II (1941–1945)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1898%E2%80%931946)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Japanese occupation and World War II (1941–1945)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Second_Philippine_Republic" title="Second Philippine Republic">Second Philippine Republic</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Surrender_of_American_troops_at_Corregidor,_Philippine_Islands,_May_1942._International_News_Photos._-_NARA_-_535554.tif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Surrender_of_American_troops_at_Corregidor%2C_Philippine_Islands%2C_May_1942._International_News_Photos._-_NARA_-_535554.tif/lossy-page1-220px-Surrender_of_American_troops_at_Corregidor%2C_Philippine_Islands%2C_May_1942._International_News_Photos._-_NARA_-_535554.tif.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="234" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Surrender_of_American_troops_at_Corregidor%2C_Philippine_Islands%2C_May_1942._International_News_Photos._-_NARA_-_535554.tif/lossy-page1-330px-Surrender_of_American_troops_at_Corregidor%2C_Philippine_Islands%2C_May_1942._International_News_Photos._-_NARA_-_535554.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Surrender_of_American_troops_at_Corregidor%2C_Philippine_Islands%2C_May_1942._International_News_Photos._-_NARA_-_535554.tif/lossy-page1-440px-Surrender_of_American_troops_at_Corregidor%2C_Philippine_Islands%2C_May_1942._International_News_Photos._-_NARA_-_535554.tif.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2824" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Surrender_of_American_troops_at_Corregidor,_Philippine_Islands,_May_1942._International_News_Photos._-_NARA_-_535554.tif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Surrender of Filipino and American troops at Corregidor, Philippine Islands, May 1942.</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Military_history_of_the_Philippines_during_World_War_II" title="Military history of the Philippines during World War II">Military history of the Philippines during World War II</a></div>
<p>A few hours after the Japanese <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">attack on Pearl Harbor</a> on December 7, 1941, the Japanese launched air raids in several cities and US military installations in the Philippines on December 8, and on December 10, the first Japanese troops landed in Northern <a href="/wiki/Luzon" title="Luzon">Luzon</a>. Filipino pilot Captain <a href="/wiki/Jes%C3%BAs_A._Villamor" title="Jesús A. Villamor">Jesús A. Villamor</a>, leading a flight of three <a href="/wiki/Boeing_P-26_Peashooter" title="Boeing P-26 Peashooter">P-26</a> "Peashooter" fighters of the 6th Pursuit Squadron, distinguished himself by attacking two enemy formations of 27 planes each and downing a much-superior Japanese <a href="/wiki/A6M_Zero" class="mw-redirect" title="A6M Zero">Zero</a>, for which he was awarded the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Distinguished_Service_Cross_(United_States)" title="Distinguished Service Cross (United States)">Distinguished Service Cross</a>. The two other planes in that flight, flown by Lieutenants <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A9sar_Basa" title="César Basa">César Basa</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Geronimo_Aclan&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Geronimo Aclan (page does not exist)">Geronimo Aclan</a>, were shot down.<sup id="cite_ref-Zaide1994ch25p325_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zaide1994ch25p325-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>General <a href="/wiki/Douglas_MacArthur" title="Douglas MacArthur">Douglas MacArthur</a>, commander of the United States Armed Forces in the Far East (USAFFE), was forced to retreat to Bataan. Manila was occupied by the Japanese on January 2, 1942. The fall of Bataan was on April 9, 1942 with <a href="/wiki/Corregidor_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Corregidor Island">Corregidor Island</a>, at the mouth of Manila Bay, surrendering on May 6.<sup id="cite_ref-Zaide1994ch25pp329-331_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zaide1994ch25pp329-331-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:184px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jouge_B_Vargas_and_Homma_Masaharu.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Jouge_B_Vargas_and_Homma_Masaharu.jpg/182px-Jouge_B_Vargas_and_Homma_Masaharu.jpg" decoding="async" width="182" height="307" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Jouge_B_Vargas_and_Homma_Masaharu.jpg/273px-Jouge_B_Vargas_and_Homma_Masaharu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Jouge_B_Vargas_and_Homma_Masaharu.jpg/364px-Jouge_B_Vargas_and_Homma_Masaharu.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2058" data-file-height="3467" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jouge_B_Vargas_and_Homma_Masaharu.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Meeting of <a href="/wiki/Jorge_B._Vargas" title="Jorge B. Vargas">Jorge B. Vargas</a>, a secretary of President Manuel Quezon, and Homma Masaharu, a General Lieutenant of the Imperial Japanese Army on February, 20th 1943</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jose_Laurel.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Jose_Laurel.JPG/220px-Jose_Laurel.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Jose_Laurel.JPG/330px-Jose_Laurel.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Jose_Laurel.JPG/440px-Jose_Laurel.JPG 2x" data-file-width="490" data-file-height="653" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jose_Laurel.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_P._Laurel" class="mw-redirect" title="José P. Laurel">José P. Laurel</a> Became the President of the Philippines during the Japanese occupation</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:General_Yamashita_Surrenders.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/General_Yamashita_Surrenders.jpg/220px-General_Yamashita_Surrenders.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="281" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/General_Yamashita_Surrenders.jpg/330px-General_Yamashita_Surrenders.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/General_Yamashita_Surrenders.jpg/440px-General_Yamashita_Surrenders.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4719" data-file-height="6024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:General_Yamashita_Surrenders.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>General <a href="/wiki/Tomoyuki_Yamashita" title="Tomoyuki Yamashita">Tomoyuki Yamashita</a> surrenders to the Filipino soldiers and guerrillas in the presence of Generals <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Mayhew_Wainwright_IV" class="mw-redirect" title="Jonathan Mayhew Wainwright IV">Jonathan Wainwright</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Percival" title="Arthur Percival">Arthur Percival</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The Commonwealth government by then had exiled itself to Washington, DC, upon the invitation of President Roosevelt; however many politicians stayed behind and collaborated with the occupying Japanese. The <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Commonwealth_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Philippine Commonwealth Army">Philippine Commonwealth Army</a> continued to fight the Japanese in a <a href="/wiki/Guerrilla_warfare" title="Guerrilla warfare">guerrilla</a> war and were considered auxiliary units of the United States Army. Several Philippine Commonwealth military awards, such as the <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Defense_Medal" title="Philippine Defense Medal">Philippine Defense Medal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Independence_Medal" title="Philippine Independence Medal">Independence Medal</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Liberation_Medal" title="Philippine Liberation Medal">Liberation Medal</a>, were awarded to both the United States and Philippine Armed Forces.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:289px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Douglas_MacArthur_lands_Leyte1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Douglas_MacArthur_lands_Leyte1.jpg/287px-Douglas_MacArthur_lands_Leyte1.jpg" decoding="async" width="287" height="215" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Douglas_MacArthur_lands_Leyte1.jpg/431px-Douglas_MacArthur_lands_Leyte1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Douglas_MacArthur_lands_Leyte1.jpg/574px-Douglas_MacArthur_lands_Leyte1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1199" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Douglas_MacArthur_lands_Leyte1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Gen. Douglas MacArthur wades ashore during initial landings at Leyte, Philippine Islands.</div></div></div>
