<p>As the Japanese forces advanced, Manila was declared an <a href="/wiki/Open_city" title="Open city">open city</a> to prevent it from destruction, meanwhile, the government was moved to <a href="/wiki/Corregidor" title="Corregidor">Corregidor</a>. In March 1942, General MacArthur and President Quezon fled the country. Guerrilla units harassed the Japanese when they could, and on Luzon native resistance was strong enough that the Japanese never did get control of a large part of the island. The <a href="/wiki/Hukbalahap" title="Hukbalahap">Hukbalahap</a>, a communist guerilla movement formed by peasant farmers in Central Luzon, did most of the fighting. The Hukbalahap, also known as Huks, resisted invaders and punished the people who collaborated with the Japanese, but did not have a well-disciplined organization, and were later seen as a threat to the Manila government.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Before MacArthur came back, the effectiveness of the guerilla movement had decimated Japanese control, limiting it to only 12 out of the 48 provinces.
</p><p>In October 1944, MacArthur had gathered enough additional troops and supplies to begin the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Leyte" title="Battle of Leyte">retaking of the Philippines</a>, landing with <a href="/wiki/Sergio_Osme%C3%B1a" title="Sergio Osmeña">Sergio Osmeña</a> who had assumed the Presidency after Quezon's death. The <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Constabulary" title="Philippine Constabulary">Philippine Constabulary</a> went on active service under the Philippine Commonwealth Army on October 28, 1944 during liberation under the Commonwealth regime. The battles entailed long fierce fighting; some of the Japanese continued to fight until the official surrender of the Empire of Japan on September 2, 1945.<sup id="cite_ref-Zaide1994ch25pp323-335_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zaide1994ch25pp323-335-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After their landing, Filipino and American forces also undertook measures to suppress the <a href="/wiki/Hukbalahap" title="Hukbalahap">Huk movement</a>, which was founded to fight the Japanese Occupation. The Filipino and American forces removed local Huk governments and imprisoned many high-ranking members of the Philippine Communist Party. While these incidents happened, there was still fighting against the Japanese forces and, despite the American and Philippine measures against the Huk, they still supported American and Filipino soldiers in the fight against the Japanese.
</p><p>Over a million Filipinos (including regular and constable soldiers, recognized guerrillas and non-combatant civilians) had been killed in the war.  The 1947 final report of the  High Commissioner to the Philippines documents massive damage to most coconut mills and sugar mills;  inter-island  shipping had all been destroyed or removed; concrete highways had been broken up for use on military airports; railways were inoperative; Manila was 80 percent destroyed, Cebu 90 percent, and Zamboanga 95 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Independence_.281946.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_(1946)">Independence (1946)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1898%E2%80%931946)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Independence (1946)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Philippine_Independence,_July_4_1946.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Philippine_Independence%2C_July_4_1946.jpg/220px-Philippine_Independence%2C_July_4_1946.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="304" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Philippine_Independence%2C_July_4_1946.jpg/330px-Philippine_Independence%2C_July_4_1946.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Philippine_Independence%2C_July_4_1946.jpg/440px-Philippine_Independence%2C_July_4_1946.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="1770" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Philippine_Independence,_July_4_1946.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Philippine Independence, July 4, 1946 from all the Colonizers. The Flag of the United States of America is lowered while the Flag of the Philippines is raised.</div></div></div>
<p>Philippine independence came on July 4, 1946, with the signing of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Manila_(1946)" title="Treaty of Manila (1946)">Treaty of Manila</a> between the governments of the United States and the Philippines. The treaty provided for the recognition of the independence of the Republic of the Philippines and the relinquishment of American sovereignty over the Philippine Islands.<sup id="cite_ref-UN254_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN254-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> From 1946 to 1961, Independence Day was observed on July 4. On 12 May 1962, President Macapagal issued Presidential Proclamation No. 28, proclaiming Tuesday, June 12, 1962 as a special public holiday throughout the Philippines.<sup id="cite_ref-bibingka-jun12_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bibingka-jun12-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> In 1964, Republic Act No. 4166 changed the date of Independence Day from July 4 to June 12 and renamed the July 4 holiday as Philippine Republic Day.<sup id="cite_ref-RA4166_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RA4166-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II_veteran_benefits">World War II veteran benefits</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_Philippines_(1898%E2%80%931946)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: World War II veteran benefits">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>During World War II, over 200,000 Filipinos fought in defense of the United States against the Japanese in the Pacific theater of military operations, where more than half died. As a commonwealth of the United States before and during the war, Filipinos were legally American nationals. With American nationality, Filipinos were promised all the benefits afforded to those serving in the armed forces of the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-pbspage_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbspage-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> In 1946, Congress passed the <a href="/wiki/Rescission_Act_of_1946" title="Rescission Act of 1946">Rescission Act</a> (<a href="/wiki/Title_38_of_the_United_States_Code" title="Title 38 of the United States Code">38 U.S.C.</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/38/107">§&#160;107</a>) which stripped Filipinos of the benefits they were promised.<sup id="cite_ref-pbspage_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbspage-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since the passage of the Rescission Act, many Filipino veterans have traveled to the United States to lobby Congress for the benefits promised to them for their service and sacrifice. Over 30,000 of such veterans live in the United States today, with most being United States citizens. Sociologists introduced the phrase "Second Class Veterans" to describe the plight of these Filipino Americans. Beginning in 1993, numerous bills titled <a href="/wiki/Filipino_Veterans_Fairness_Act" title="Filipino Veterans Fairness Act">Filipino Veterans Fairness Act</a> were introduced in Congress to return the benefits taken away from these veterans, only to die in committee. The <a href="/wiki/American_Recovery_and_Reinvestment_Act_of_2009" title="American Recovery and Reinvestment Act of 2009">American Recovery and Reinvestment Act of 2009</a>, signed into law on February 17, 2009, included provisions to pay benefits to the 15,000 remaining veterans.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On January 6, 2011 <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Speier" title="Jackie Speier">Jackie Speier</a> (D-CA), U.S. Representative for <span data-sort-value="California12&#160;!"><a href="/wiki/California%27s_12th_congressional_district" title="California&#39;s 12th congressional district">California's 12th congressional district</a></span>, serving since 2008, introduced a bill seeking to make Filipino WW-II veterans eligible for the same benefits available to U.S. veterans. In a news conference to outline the bill, Speier estimated that approximately 50,000 Filipino veterans survive.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
